GAME: Last Night on Earth: The Zombie Game
RANK: 530
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I wanted to love it, but I didn't.  It took much longer than it should have.  Most of the game wasn't exciting.  There was far too much luck.  Some cards were massively overpowered, some were useless.
Maybe it was the scenario we played. Or maybe it was because we had 4 players.
I'd give it another go.

Update: played twice more the basic scenario, 2 players.  It was still highly luck dependent, but it was fun.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.8
This game, plus its expansions, is the game I love to play over and over. It oozes theme, and gives my wife and I something to play that pits us against each other, or, if there are more people playing, work together towards a common goal. I still tell stories about events that have taken place within this game. It is my favorite game, and while I've been looking for something to take its place, it's hard to replace.

My only nits with this game are that it takes a long time to set up and there isn't a solo campaign. Otherwise, it is the perfect game for me.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This game was at one time my most played game. Good quality components and an engaging theme that really recreate the look and feel of a zombie film. I thought there were some balance issues in the beginning, but these are not so bad if the characters really look at their options, and develop a strategy they all can agree on from the beginning of the game. This game plays like a dungeon crawl, but with the halls of the dungeon replaced by the buildings in the town of Woodinvale. There are some very intense moments, and it always feels as if the heroes are right on the brink of death. Playing the zombie player in the base game is fun, but definitely not as fun as being a hero. (Expansions fix this to some degree, especially Survival of the fittest.) If you like zombie movies, zombie books and well.....zombie everything else....Buy this game 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

---
Had a chance to play this one again over Halloween weekend.  The main problem in the game is that the time to choice ratio is way off.  In a 2 hour game, I had 10 turns that took less than a minute to conclude.  Even worse, most of the player's "choices" are usually incredibly obvious.  I like zombies just as much as the next guy, but the theme is completely lost in the minutia of this game.

RATING: 9
Lots of fun strategies for the heroes and the zombie players. Our battle was epic and totally felt like we were in a grindhouse movie running for our lives. The cards, board spaces, and weapons give this a great flavor besides fun game play. The large squares in the middle are a great touch for movement. If your in the open, you feel like you can outrun the zombies to get where you want. but if your in a building, and zombies are blocking your exits, you really have to battle your way out or you need help fast.

RATING: 5.5

This is that game she judged Claustrophobia against. She likes the fact that in combat both parties roll dice, in claustrophobia the defending character has a stat which determines if the dice roll is a hit or miss. She also likes the cards which add variability like weapons and special abilities very frequently. Overall great zombie game.

RATING: 4
You will probably need a Zombie or two to play the zombies after the first scenario, whilst the heroes will be enjoyed by your average brain-dead gamer. Very simplistic man-to-man combat. Good production values. Perhaps mainly for the young and/or non-gamers. The CD was a nice touch, or would have been if the music on it was related to the playing experience. 
A second play of the basic game scenario suggests something is wrong somewhere, as this will not be won by four heroes unless they are heavily tooled up at game start. This seems unlikely to vary. The advanced game and cards may change things, however it makes me wonder about the quality of the testing, if any, like that's unusual.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A very fun game. LNOE succeeds where nearly every other game in this genre has failed. It's thematic, has a reasonable play length, multiple scenarios, low down time, excellent production values, clean rules, etc, etc. It's not trying to be the next Caylus, but if you are looking for a zombie game and feel that a heavy dose of luck fits well with the genre, then I don't think you'll find a better candidate. Extra points for the nice combination of cooperation and player vs. player.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I played 2 scenarios of this: the one involving getting escaping by pickup truck and the one about defending the manor.
This has a lot of similarities to [thing=35815]A Touch of Evil[/thing], especially in the production values.
What I liked: the high quality of the cards.  The short game play.  The plastic.  Some of the card text (notably teenage angst and the card that gave the game its name).
What I didn't like: It seemed imbalanced in favor of the zombies.  
I think if the heroes beat the zombie with only 1 die, they fought them off, but if they win with 2 dice, they kill the zombie.  In two games, I never saw a zombie die by rolling doubles.  It's just too difficult.
Also, theme and rules didn't intersect at one point.  As the zombie player, I played "locked door" on two of his characters and locked them into the gym.  My zombies would burst in and attack, but after killing the zombies, the heroes could not leave.  Huh?  You can't walk through that big hole in the wall or floor?  That play was a game changer.
Overall, though, I think there it was a good game.  The combat system might need a little tweaking to bring balance, or maybe I just didn't play enough games.  It was a good enough game that I would like to play it again, and if I do, I will revise comments and ratings accordingly.

RATING: 8.5
Oh how AnotherHorrorFan loves this game. Really effectively conveys the zombie feel. I convinced a friend to get the game, without playing it with me first, and he proceeded to hate it. After talking with him I found he was playing with a number of rules wrong, namely; deciding to search before rolling, and more than one zombie card played per fight. RATING: 7.5

The game is nice, especially the miniatures which add to an overall super good quality, but the game play is pretty simplistic. As human, not much to do other than ... kill zombies or be wounded or killed by them. Not many items, not many combos, just shoot or hit and wait for dawn. RATING: 8
Sep-30-2007
Wow.  What a fun game.  This is an experience game and not very strategic, which is fine.  The choices are very simple but it is great fun!  The game really unfolds just like a horror movie.  The heroes start out away from each other as they frantically search for items to help them survive.  As the game goes on, they realize there are other people in town trying to stay alive as well and band together to increase their chances until they finally win.  I love the fact that the system is so flexible that this game can be expanded ad infinitum.  It is also great that the game is scenario driven so each game will feel differently on top of the crazy things that happen in the game.  Hands down, this is the BEST EXPERIENCE-TYPE GAME.  This is what Arkham Horror and Fury of Dracula should have been.  Turns are very fast that keeps the action going and the experience moving.  Overall, just a lot of fun!  I have been waiting for a game like this to augment my Heavy-Strategy biased collection.

RATING: 8
My wife and I have been enjoying playing this game 2 player. The first time my wife played, she got a little frustrated with it. But once she started thinking about it as a zombie movie being played out as a board game, she's had a lot more fun with it.
It seems that this game is really about how well the heroes can work together versus how well the zombie player can play their cards. There are some tactical decisions to be made. Nothing real brain burning by any means, but enough to make it fun. And that's really what this game is about, I think. Having a fun experience whether you win or lose. At one point, I was rooting for my hero to get turned into a zombie, just so it would happen. That's the kind of game it is.
I think my only concern is with the limited number of scenarios.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
Positives: Simple mechanics, fun (mostly the cinematic quality of the game: a few survivors holding out against an army of zombies where bad luck is in inevitable, while the smallest piece of luck could bring on victory), (to emphasize) very good theme, nice bits.

Negatives: Scary theme (as noted in at least one review: not suitable for children or people who are easily frightened).  The luck factor can be a problem if you're looking for much strategy or control (of course this game is set up with the theme of heroes who can't seem to get a break).  Some of the cards can up the learning curve (nothing out of the range of your average CCG, though).  Might get kind of boring playing the zombies sometimes.

Plays: 
2-player: 3
3-player: 3 (2nd game Zombies squashed the heroes because they couldn't find weapons or get die rolls as consistently as the zombies)
4-player: 1 (played with only three hero characters. Result: Routed Heroes. Probably will be more balance with the full compliment.)

RATING: 7
A thrilling survival game featuring -surprise- zombies!

Move your stereotypical survivor around in town in order to find mission relevant items or just to kill zombies. 

One or two players take over the control of the zombies the others play the survivors. 

The zombie-side gets the usual helping scenarios like "lights going out", "survivors panicking" and "locked doors without reason".
The survivors get weapons and gear to deplete the plague.
As usual there is more zombies than weapons in the beginning and sooner or later, one of the player gets bitten and eventually turns into a zombie before whatever task is done - you know: the works.

Played it with fans of the genre and I liked it a lot.

RATING: 7
This is one of the first zombie games I ever played, and while i still like it, a few years ago my review would likely have been more glowing. The art style of this game looks like pictures of actors in a b-movie which seemed clever at first, but over time I got tired of it. Of this style of game, I like recent ones more, especially those that forego someone controlling the zombies and instead have a natural system for their movement, because ultimately in this game the zombie player doesn't really have that many choices to make. It's pretty clear to all what the best thing to do is most of the time for them. This is also true of the humans, and often i find the strategy to be to hide in a room until you can find what you need in the deck. While this makes a great deal of sense thematically, this particular occurrence doesn't make for exciting gameplay. 

Still a very good game that I'd be happy to play, but given the choice, I'd go with zombicide black plague, or maybe dead of winter.

RATING: N/A
 Gift from Bob
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I don’t like zombie games: they all feel the same, a cheap and unoriginal jumble of the same stale concepts. Yet today zombies are even trendier, so much they keep coming in all kinds of ways. So imagine my  excitement when I was asked to play Last Night on Earth, despite the cool miniatures that come with the game: yet I changed my mind soon after this game started as it’s lots of fun.

To begin with, its rules are very simple both to teach and understand: you grasp the basics quickly, then you keep improving your playing as the game progresses. In the second place, the semi-cooperative nature of the game - that lets a player control the zombies and the others play as the humans - makes it more challenging and changing every time you play: even the different - and thematically inspired - decks for the zombie and human players help have a very open game. Then, your goal isn’t simply «survive a fixed number of turns» or «kill all the humans» but you also have to actively do something, even if it’s something as easy as killing the most zombies you can or scare the hell out of the characters. Finally, all the materials are high-quality, which is always a win in my book.

I have no idea how the many expansions work, whether they are worthy and, in case, which of them are not to be missed, as I didn’t try out any of them: I did play the basic game only and I deeply enjoyed my time with it.

RATING: 6
I like the game -- there is nothing quite like it in my collection, and the game is very thematic and fun.  My inclination is to give it an 8.  However, there can be a lot of downtime, especially if there are two zombie players and they have to coordinate with each other.  The event cards can also make the game very frustrating, especially for the heroes. 

Another complaint is that the way the hero deck is stacked at the beginning, not the decisions the players make, is the main determining factor in whether the heroes win or lose.  Well, this is no different than many cooperative games.  You just have to approach it as a story being told and not as a battle of wits.

Still a really fun game.  I like Betrayal at House on the Hill, too, but for most people I'd recommend this game over that.  They aren't trying to do the same thing, exactly, but for most people it isn't worth it to seek out Betrayal if LNoE is readily available.  LNoE is the better game.

No expansions are required, but Growing Hunger and Survival of the Fittest (in that order) are worth it for exploring further.

RATING: 10
I love this game even though it hates me. I love how each play is like scripting out a B-grade zombie movie. One of the best implementations of a theme that I've seen thus far. Love the components. The die rolls for movement and combat can be and are brutal (oh man I lose so much) and a lot of the cardplay can be frustratingly ambiguous, resulting in a lot of house ruling for us, but I love the theme, which goes a long way toward overlooking the flaws. The ability to come up with your own scenarios is a big plus. Majority of plays have been 2 player, one controlling the zombies and the other controlling four heroes, although two of them were with four (three hero players, one controlling two heroes, and one zombie player) - changes the dynamic of the game a lot when you have more people plotting on how to kill the zombies.

A great game for when I'm out at the lake with buddies, as we're all quite fond of the Zombie theme and the mechanics are decent enough.  My regular group does not play it much, as we prefer Zombies!!! for a fast-paced zombie horror game.

RATING: 3
I will preface this review in that I played the zombie side in this game and even though I won, this game was very frustrating and boring.  As the zombies you draw cards and if you draw something good you can play it, else you move one space and that's it.  Then you wait while the heroes move around up to 6 spaces depending on a die roll and search to find new gear and new items.  Then it's the zombie turn again, draw so cards, move one space, back to the heroes.  It was incredibly boring playing the zombies and I knew exactly what we needed to do to win, kill two survivors, but because of the huge disparity in movement it could have dragged on for the entire game if not for some lucky card draws.  Which that also annoys me, if you don't draw good cards, you aren't going to accomplish anything.  So in the end this game is a hard pass for me, maybe I might play as the heroes next times but I will never play the zombies again.

RATING: 9
This is, by far, one of my favorite games!  Although it may start out slow, the overall effect, once combined with the expansions, is superb!  On its own, the game feels as if it's missing "something."  Despite that, it's simple enough to play, with rules that hide their complexity quite well.  

Visually, the game is great!  I could do with a less "cartoony" feel to the board, but it serves its purpose quite well.  The minis are solid, and easy to paint, which was a good thing, because the Heroes became hard to distinguish from each other during the first few game sessions.  Apply a bit of character with a brush, and suddenly, everything pops!

I would have given the game a much higher score, but the financial investment required to achieve its potential for greatness demands that I lower the score a bit.

WORD OF ADVICE:  The game is best played when using a scenario that does not require the Heroes to search through the deck for specific items.  "Defend the Manor House" has to be the best scenario the base game has to offer.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Almost an instant Ameritrash classic, this game is NOT an innovative, ingenious, or "clever" revision of what we've come to expect from the problematic zombie game genre- despite reports to the contrary, the game isn't a complete 180 from the type of gameplay in ZOMBIES and in fact LNoE very much resembles a "fixed" version of that game with a more reasonable scenario structure, a cooperation element, and an overall richer game experience.  Where LNoE succeeds the most is in bringing the accessibility and atmospheric narrative of BETRAYAL AT THE HOUSE ON THE HILL to the zombie genre and the result is a tremendously playable, fast-paced game that will likely have a great deal of crossover appeal and market penetration.  The rules are simple (despite some crude grammar and syntax in the rulebook), easy to teach and there is a sense of directness and immediacy that is both engaging and endearing- this is a very meat-and-potatoes game without a bunch of mechanical folderol or gaminess to get in the way of undead antics.  The modular setup is nice but restrictive, the scenarios are fun and the potential for more is great, and as a whole the game is a lot of fun particularly in its 60-80 minute duration.  I'm not a huge fan of the setting (I prefer the more urban, militaristic zombie millieu than the rural one offered by the game)and I think the artwork is absolutely awful- I'd much rather have some nice FFG-quality illustrations than photographs with slapped-on Photoshop filters).  The miniatures are nice and almost counteract the sticky, cheaply printed cards but as a whole it's a good first production for Flying Frog.  The CD is a stupid gimmick undoubtedly the result of the designer having a musician friend and frankly they should have invested that money in either a better artist, nicer production, or just knocked a couple of bucks off the MSRP.  In all, I think LNoE is an exceptional horror game and I expect that it'll be around for many years to come- it has that "X" factor that games like BETRAYAL have that guarantee that even if the NOTRE DAME set doesn't take to it, then thousands of other people will.

RATING: 10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
The Greatest Zombie Game of All Time! This game just drips theme, zombie putrescent theme! :zombie:

The combat system has a simple elegance to it that seems to capture the spirit of a zombie movie. Simply winning a combat against zombies is not enough to kill them, but merely "fends" them off. You need to roll doubles and beat them in order to win. It really invokes an image of the heroes trying to break free of the zombies as they claw and grab at them.

The components are first class especially for the first game from a new gaming company.

I love the haters of this game and their bitching about randomness, the lack of strategy, balance issues, and that players can get in situations where they are completely out of control of their character. Seriously, what were you expecting? It is a FUCKING B-MOVIE STYLE ZOMBIE GAME! It is not trying to be Age of Steam for fucks sake! This is a game of pure theme. If you don't like to roll dice then go play Caylus. As for lack of strategy, that is bullshit. There is plenty of strategies and tactics available to the players if you can actually get past the fact that this is not a perfect information game like Puerto Rico and your carefully laid plan may fail due the that Great Satan, Randomness. As for balance and the fact that you can get into a situation beyond your control, have you actually ever watched a horror movie? That is what this is attempting to model not bloody chess!

I have been to events where this game is being played and almost everyone is laughing and hooting as their zombies get blasted and their characters eaten. While this is going on there are others nearby playing a "deep" strategy game and it is as quiet as a tomb with everyone concentrating so deeply they look constipated. I sure as hell know which table I want to be at.

Hey, I actually like games like Caylus and Puerto Rico and they are fine when I am in the mood. But, for all out zombie apocalypse fun, this is much preferred.

A couple of things I do wish for. First I wish there was more use for the Manor House. It seems to be a waste to have that whole board taken up for only one scenario. Also, with the Manor House they should included some a way to board up windows and doors.

A quibble I have is with the board shading. I was one of the first few to buy the game. I bee lined it for Flying Frog booth at Gencon '07 to make sure I got a copy. I feel as an early adopter I got screwed when they changed the shading of the new boards in the subsequent expansion. It is not that big of a deal, but it is a minor annoyance, that I feel they should have fixed on THEIR dime. I actually did consider buying the replacements boards, but with shipping it was just silly. So, now my game looks odd when you play with the boards from the base game and the expansion.

The shading on the original boards are 10 times better than the new ones. I do not know for the life of me why they would go with those new boards with the flat greenish tint.

RATING: 4
Effectively one play.  We played one scenario and it went so horribly wrong (zombies won in three turns) that we decided to do it again.  Decided the first experience was a bit of a 'perfect storm' for the zombies (perfect cards, dice rolls) vs. the heroes (bad rolls ... something like 8 consecutive ones, useless card draws).  Second run-through of same scenario went much better.

Overall opinion was a mixed bag ... wonderful application of theme!  Tremendous components!  Exciting moments!  But the gameplay was sluggish as we referenced the rules and FAQ multiple times.  We went WELL over the 1 hour listed time and called it around the two-hour mark when it seemed like the heroes were running away with it despite the fact that there were still something like 8 turns to go.

Experience reminded me very much of Betrayal at the House on the Hill in both a good and bad way (although the rules not NEARLY as clunky as Betrayal).  After repeated play my rating for that game went up as we understood the interaction of the game's ideas and components much better ... so I imagine with repeated play my rating for LNOE would go up a bit as well.  Especially if the play time fits into that one-hour projection.

*update* actually knocked this down a point after playing Cowboys: Way of the Gun - similar game that has all the elements I love in LNOE, and a theme I enjoy more, but it has less clunkiness.  Would rather play Cowboys.

RATING: 7
Last Night on Earth has some flaws, but is a very enjoyable game. It's not so heavy that my family is turned off by it, and comes with different scenarios to help the game feel fresh.

My biggest problem is down time. If you play as the zombies, your turn will usually go by quickly, but the heroes will take forever. Not just that, but the game is usually very one-sided in my experience and, depending on your choice of scenario, decently luck driven.

All in all, it is an enjoyable game and I will happily play it with my family.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.85
When you're in the mood for a cooperative game but don't have the time for Arkham Horror, this is the game for you.  It's relatively light, moves fast, and is worth a lot of laughs.

Players work either on the zombie side or the human side in various scenarios, each with their own goals.  The Humans are generally trying to defeat a certain number of zombies in a given timeframe, while the zombies try to run out the clock.  Each side draws from a deck of special cards, as the players try to outmaneuver each other.  ("My zombie uses a Shamble card to race towards Sally."  "Cancel a zombie action!")

This offers just enough strategy and tension to satisfy your average gamer, but remains light enough to bring in beginners to the hobby.  Thumbs up for a game I'd gladly play whenever it's offered.

RATING: 8
A modern zombie classic for the more casual gamer - and a true hit in our household.  

Last Night on Earth is THE GAME that reintroduced me to board games after a many yeared lay off.  As such, it is also THE GAME that introduced my daughters to the true joys of the hobby. 

If there is going to be a world beyond Dog-opoly and Mille Bournes, let it be populated by brain hungry zombies.    

Flying Frog Productions has to be one of the more thematic of game publisher/designers in this new Golden Age of board gaming.  In this, their first game, the Frog absolutely nails the dread of Romero flavored zombie movies.

RATING: 8
Last Night on Earth is based on B-Zombie Horror Movies like Dawn of the Dead, Zombieland, and so on. You either play as the townsfolk heroes trying to survive the zombie apocalypse or the zombies trying to eat and kill said heroes. This game is a lot of fun to play and I had a "Heart of the Cards" moment when the heroes were about to escape and I played the "A Town Overrun" card which made the heroes deck lose ten cards and if there were no more cards in the hero deck they lost so I won that way. It has tons of expansions from what I've seen so it has lots of replay value but it still has replay value in the base game too. Also it has a cd with it that you can run in the background while playing the game which gives a much creepier atmosphere to the game.  For a zombie survival game, you can't really go wrong with Last Night on Earth.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Wow! Zombie killing goodness. When I played this for my first time, I really had a ball. I've seen other reviews that downplay the game because of the random factor, but I really enjoyed it. There were some complaints from the zombie player that this game was unbalanced in favor of the townsfolk, but then the zombies ended up winning on the last turn. It seemed to me that the game truly could have gone either way the whole time, and that makes for a good game. (IMPORTANT NOTE: the character of Father Joseph, equipped with a Faith card AND the pitchfork, is a zombie killing machine!)  Anyway, bottom line is that I really liked this game. I guess that maybe I really am an Ameritrasher, after all. Oh well - A little randomness never hurt anyone. Embrace the dice!  Love the dice!
BTW, the components are absolutely awesome looking. All the artwork on the cards is glossy photo quality, and lends an air of "realism" to the game.
A final bonus, for me - it can be played two player. (And my wife likes it!)

This was traded away, not because I didn't like it, but because it just wasn't played enough.  Plus, I grew weary of the whole zombie/occult theme.

RATING: 6
Players represent townsfolk cooperating to fight off a plague of zombies, or the zombies themselves.  Scenario driven game where players are trying to complete objectives (destroy 15 zombies, get the truck started and get out of here, etc) while trying to stay alive.  The zombie player(s) are trying to deny victory, or kill off two townsfolk.  Game mechanics are simple and intuitive - basically move/search then fight.  Combat is a bit like History of the World - roll a bunch of dice and highest single roll is your result.  Event and item cards spice things up.  Wonderful components, from the sturdy variable game boards, miniatures, cards and counters.  Looks like actors/models were hired for a zombie photo shoot for the components and the results are great.  I enjoyed this game much more than I was expecting - a zombie game where you are faced with real choices.  Good stuff.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Maybe I'm playing it wrong, but right now I don't want to play it at all. Great art and theme, though.

RATING: 2
This game looked like so much fun when it was featured on “Table Top” that when someone brought it to a game meet, I enthusiastically looked forward to playing it.  Wow, what a disappointment!  We just felt like we were going round and round in circles rolling dice hoping to hit the right numbers.  That’s basically what the game comes down to.  It calls itself a cooperative game, but it sure didn’t feel like it.  One player got eliminated and basically was sitting around twiddling his thumbs, while two other remaining characters were pent up in a corner and getting pummeled by Zombies.  I was successfully holding up my corner of the board (basically its down to lucky dice rolls, that’s all) and then our DM (I mean this really is just a role-playing game but without any good story to keep you interested) asked me if I would like to go over and help my teammates out.  I looked at the guy sitting in the corner twiddling his thumbs and replied to her, ‘hell no!  I might get myself killed doing that!’  As far as I was concerned, this was a last man standing game.  
Seriously, go play “Zombies!!!” if it’s the theme you are looking for.  That game plays faster and I remember enjoying it much better than this thing.  At least in that game you feel like you are building the board Carcassonne-style, exploring places and have more options on each turn as to what direction you want to go.  “Last Night on Earth” just drags on for way too long and you are running around and around in circles on a relatively small board.

A pretty good game marred by a horrid rule book and card text.  We had so many questions after our first two playings that we had to start a long list and begin hunting for answers.  The card text just isn't sufficient to answer simple questions that pop up. Really, most of these questions should have been obvious to the writer and included in the earliest drafts of the rule book. The others should have popped up during the earliest playtests and been incorporated into the rules long before the game went to print. More time should have been spent on this than on the fancy photos etc. since the rules themselves are absolutely necessary to play the game. All that aside, I still have fun playing this one. It's rich in theme and can get quite tense.  I'd have probably given it a 7.5 or an 8 with tighter rules and card text.

RATING: 4
Good.  A nice light game, although still heavy on rules for non-gamers.  The theme is top-notch and the team gameplay makes for some nice competition.  Great bits and hilarious stereotypes fill out the zombie-movie experience.

However ... the game really needs a streamlined, total reworking by a skilled developer.  The guys at Flying Frog have a great handle on theme and production, but their game-design inexperience shows.  A lot of the rules for weapons are inconsistent (most guns you roll after attacking to see if you're out of ammo, but the pistol is out if the attack roll is a one, etc.) and the other weapons have seemingly random effects that have little connection to the theme -- and in a game that is so reliant on theme, this is crippling.

RATING: 10
There's something about Last Night on Earth that scratches every single gaming itch I have. It's zombie-themed, for starters, and unlike Zombies!!! it's actually a lot of fun to play. The gameplay itself isn't terribly deep; most of the rules can be explained in five or ten minutes and there's an extremely helpful "rules summary" card printed for each player. But this also makes it perfect for a pickup-and-play game since you almost never have to refer back to the rulebook. I do think it's fairly ridiculous that some people complain about the length of the FAQ, because 99% of the time the correct answer to rules questions/card interactions is the obvious one. Perhaps some of that comes from my CCG background; but even the inexperienced shouldn't have too much difficulty their first time playing.

Last Night on Earth is also immensely fun. Players' turns are fast and furious, but there's a fair amount of tactical planning required as well. If you don't plan with the rest of your team, you're going to end up alone in an abandoned building with a swarm of zombies about to overtake you. I write that from the Heroes' perspective since we only ever assign one person to be the zombie player. LNoE's rulebook suggests using 2 zombie players when you have 4 or 6 people, but I think the game then loses quite a bit of enjoyment on the zombies' end. There simply isn't enough to do in order to justify splitting the zombies and their cards in two. Five players is really the maximum for Last Night on Earth--four heroes and one zombie. And that also happens to be the game's sweet spot, although I've had just as much fun with 2-4.

Combat is dice-based, but there are enough modifiers and special abilities in the game that both zombies and humans can significantly affect the outcome if they wish. Having said that, however, I can't count the number of times everything has hinged on a crucial die roll. And a player picks up a die and tosses it across the table, the cheering and yelling can be quite intense. I think that's one of Last Night on Earth's strengths: everything works to draw you into the game and become emotionally involved. This isn't one to play passively or quietly.

One of the brilliant things about LNoE is the scenario system. This, more than anything else, is what keeps the game endlessly fresh. Some of the scenarios have a similar feel, but there are enough crazy ones to keep the replay value extremely high. Right now I have a total of 11 scenarios in the game box (base game + Growing Hunger + all of the expansions). Some favor the heroes; some favor the zombies. But even if you only play each scenario several times, there's no way you're going to get tired of LNoE anytime soon.

When I first started playing, I thought the zombies had a bit of a disadvantage compared to the Heroes. Even trying my hardest, the Heroes were winning every single game, often quite easily. But then things flipped; for several games in a row the zombies were dominant. But as players figured out some of the nuances in the game (yes, they are there), the win ratio is now roughly 50-50. You can't think like a hero when you're playing the zombies, and vice versa. It also helps having a general idea of what kinds of cards are in your deck; I didn't immediately realize that the zombie player should be cycling as many cards as possible every turn to draw the ones needed. In contrast, unless the heroes need specific items for the scenario (Escape in the Truck or Burn 'Em Out!, for example) you'll want to hold onto your best cards for when they're most needed.

Last Night on Earth also has some amazing production values, comparable to anything Days of Wonder or Fantasy Flight puts out. The hero miniatures are extremely well-detailed; the modular boards (even the lighter ones) are a lot of fun to play on, and the filtered photography on all of the cards looks extremely impressive. I know there are those that would prefer actual illustrations instead of photos, but I really like the effect that Flying Frog went for--it fits the horror movie theme perfectly. (I think it works slightly less well on A Touch of Evil, but that's a different story).

In nearly all of our games now, the scenario isn't won or lost until the final turn or two. This causes a lot of tension when we play since it's never obvious who's going to win. And the narrative structure of the game lends itself so well to telling stories about your experiences with LNoE; I don't know how often we've been playing a different game when someone pipes up with "Remember the time when the sheriff sacrificed himself to lure some zombies away from the farmhouse? Then Jenny moved six spaces across the board and threw a fire extinguisher into the farmhouse to push all of the zombies left in there outside so Sally could run in with the weapons. Oh wow, that was fun!"

People genuinely love this game. It's fast-paced, thematic, tactical, and deliciously tense. Last Night on Earth has become one of my favorite games to play, and I don't expect to grow tired of it for a long time to come (perhaps never, if Flying Frog keeps releasing expansions). That is one downside, though; a $50 base game quickly becomes $150 after all of the expansions and extra zombies--with more on the way. But I gave up on the Battlelore system a long time ago, and I've gladly handed over the title of "King of the Expandable Game" to Flying Frog. 

[b]Edit[/b]: There is one bad thing about LNoE: the soundtrack CD that comes with the game. It's unfortunately one of those things that's great on paper but poor in execution. I love the idea of having a soundtrack; it really fits in well with LNoE's desire to be an immersive gaming experience. But the CD comes across as rather hokey and kind of boring. I applaud Flying Frog's efforts; but neither this game nor A Touch of Evil really needs its own soundtrack.

RATING: 9
I've had some epic sessions of LNOE, and it remains a game that I enjoy playing on occasion for the memorable moments it creates. The game does an amazing job creating the experience of being in your own zombie movie. Throw in a touch of roleplaying and you can have a blast.

We have memories of a character sacrificing themself so others could get away -- and then fighting off a hoard with incredible die rolls and surviving. [i]Surprised to see me? I couldn't let you guys have all the fun.[/i] Or two characters sharing a special moment in spite of the advancing threat. [i]Here, let me show you how to hold this gun. [/i] Or the bickering b*tch fight between two teens. [i]No, YOU'RE a slut![/i] It's a house rule that you have to say your character's catch-phrase at least once, and you have to yell, [i]I'll see you in hell![/i] when throwing the dynamite. 

It's a fragile design, for sure, and you can have some wipeouts. Especially annoying is the roll-for-movement, but these flaws don't override the fact that you can have epic sessions with this game unlike any other -- zombie game or not. I highly recommend The Growing Hunger expansion for the additional elements it offers and the point balancing system. A must-have if you're going to invest in this gaming system.

RATING: 4
Goofy B-movie horror.  No good with two, three, or four in my experience.  Can occasionally be lots of fun with five. 

Played one game that culminated in an incredible ending where the humans were holed up in the same building, dramatically fending off a hoard of zombies just as dawn approached. Two humans were dragged from the building to be eaten alive, but just when the situation seemed bleakest, a surprise flame-thrower and a lucky roll allowed the survivors to hold on just long enough to see daylight. That game ended in a ragged roar of screaming and cheers and I think that's how I'd like every board game in this genre to end. That alone tempts me to bump the rating, but every other play that's ended with  unspectacular results keeps it down.  

Still, decent to break out around Halloween. It's not a good game, but from time to time it captures a good story-telling moment.

RATING: 6
I really don't want to shit on this game because zombie games are a good idea and the production value on this is pretty solid. Regardless, LNOE is very theme-driven, with the entire game being decided largely on random dice rolls and random card draws. You really have to get into the story of it in order to gloss over the fact that this is no different than Risk-style mechanics. Sure, it's not trying to be anything greater than what it is (a zombie-killing love-fest) but ultimately I feel that it is the random elements that completely decide the game rather than any input of mine in terms of strategy or meaningful decisions. A game like this should be able to balance strategy and luck through a selection of meaningful choices and ways to mitigate bad luck in a planned fashion. That rather large point aside, it still works as a tense game.

RATING: 9
Echo echo...  We love this game! The whole thing comes together very well for a great zombie bashing (or human munching) time by all who have played. After a handful of games I can say this one will definitely be hitting the table many times for years to come. This game does not replace TWC Zombies!!! for us, it does not replace Betrayal at House on the Hill for us, it also does not replace Zombie Plague for us, but it does seem to merge very well the different aspects of those games that we really seem to love! I like the expandability, the scenario mechanic, the artwork (I'm a b-movie junkie too), the game flow and timeframe designed into the game. 

The only real gripe I have is with the cards. I like the art and all, but those suckers were almost glued together. Luckily I had read on here about slightly flexing and twisting the deck and they all seemed to come apart ok. We had a couple in the zombie deck that the plastic delaminated a little on (no biggie) and the top card of one of the decks was actually not sitting square on the stack when they were shrink wrapped so it got creased over the edge a bit. I think the heat from that evil shrink wrap is what caused the plastic coated cards to stick together like that.

After getting into the scenarios more and seeing how the support for the game goes I will re-visit this rating and see if it goes up or down a point. You see, it can only go as high as a 10, which with good support and growth of the game from the publisher, it should. If it doesn't get supported and goes stale it still deserves no lower than an 8 from us for what it offers as is.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
I think that second to Nightfall, Last Night on Earth is the 2nd worst game I've ever played. Mechanically it's very similar to Betrayal at House on the Hill (which I also dislike a great deal), but characters only have 1 or 2 hit points before they die. There are no meaningful decisions here, it's just roll the dice, draw a card and maybe roll the dice again with no way to mitigate bad dice rolls at all.

While I understand that this game is meant to be more thematic than mechanic, there just doesn't seem to be any real substance here as there aren't any meaningful decisions to be made. You roll the dice, move to a spot where the zombies hopefully can't get to you, then wait. Then the zombies either don't get to you so you do it again, or they do get to you and you roll more dice to find out if you get hit or not. Most of our game was trying to just stay out of the way of the zombies while the one character with a ranged weapon tried to kill them one-by-one. How is this supposed to be fun? I just don't understand...

RATING: 8
This game combines a cooperative game (the hero players work together) with a competitive game (one or two players play the zombies) that uses interesting card play by zombies and heroes to simulate the feeling of playing out the events in a zombie horror movie. Each hero has their own special abilities which provides variety, the game comes with five different scenarios each with a different set of victory conditions, and the game board, which represents the small town that is being overrun by the zombies, is modular and randomly constructed at the beginning of each game. Dice rolling is the core mechanic here, for both movement of heroes and combat, but taken in it's entirely the game really oozes theme, has great replay value, and is fun. To add to the horror movie theme the box includes a CD of original, appropriately ominous, music to accompany the game as you play.

RATING: 9
in my opinion, one of the best zombie games out there. I would give to it an 8 even with only the vanilla things , but my final vote is 9 cause of expansions pack that I greatly reccomend for this game, giving to it lot's of variety and deepness. Last night on Earth is a semicooperative zombie games, one of the fews that gives to a player the role of the zombies trying to kill the little group of survivors trying to struggle for their lives. This is a scenario based zombie game in wich survivors must complete specifical tasks while trying to survive the hordes of zombies infected by an unknown source. the game also features a modular  L shaped based board in which at the center we have a square and at the corners we have the L shaped boards that are randomly placed in order to create a different map for every playthrough. LNOE also features scavenging sistems and with expansions you will even face different tipes of special zombies(like in every respectfull game of this genre)and even barricades sistems. recommended with 5 players, but also enjoyable with less, even with 2 players

Also, dislike how zombies can pass through walls -- the fun of zombie survival is barricading!

RATING: 9

All the cliche's are here (I won't spoil them for you), the game is well produced with modular game boards and over a dozen different scenarios out of the box. The game is largely card driven and uses dice for combat, so if your friends don't want to play a game where there is any luck in the game just tell them to stay home and calculate PI to a few more digits instead of having fun. :)  This is one of the few games that women like to play too so that might scare off some of the recluse gamers (warn them in advance). :)  My rating might go up to 10 on this one but I want to have a chance to play more games of this with different groups of different sizes.

RATING: 4
Cannot get a better theme for me. Some places the gameplay doesn't quite fit the theme (zombies move around intelligently, protecting the house is easier from the outside), but usually I feel like I am in a city being attacked by zombies.

The last 30 mins. of most of our games have been a dull.

RATING: 5
[DEC 08] [Rating: 7]
This is not really my type of game as it has a roll and move aspect, there is a lot of take that aspect to the game. Still, I quite enjoyed this game anyway. The theme is well integrated to the game and it feels just like a college zombie flick and the soundtrack is nice when played on low volume. There is a certain feel of angst when taking the decisions and even if the zombies are quite dumb, there is certainly a lot of strategy behind what long term decisions to take to hinder the humans. I played my first game with the advanced rules and I think they work great and I suspect that they are much better than the beginning rules set.

The feel of the game is that it is very tactical and while I can agree on that premise, there is certainly strategic options, especially for the zombie player. It isn’t fun to be stuck with all your zombies in one corner of the map, because they are slow.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Cool theme; easy to learn; fast-paced play.  Game mechanics lend themselves well to the zombie-movie feel.  The turns go fairly quick, and players have minimal idle time.  Quality products: nice looking map, cards, pictures and other game components (Although, my cards came stuck together in a block). Players can get through the five scenarios fairly quickly.  Thus, the game has the potential of quickly becoming rote.  On the other hand, new scenarios, characters, and map sections can easily be added to the game.  On the down side, random cards and zombie spawn rolls can greatly change game balance of any scenario; One game can be close while the next game of the same scenario can be a blow-out for either side.  I don't enjoy a lopsided game, even if I am on the winning side.  All-in-all, a fun, light, fast-paced game for those who like the zombie theme.

RATING: 10
I'd had my eye on this game for a while and finally got a chance to play. It did not disappoint. I loved the team aspect, I loved the components, and it is dripping with theme. The CD is a take-it-or-leave-it thing for me. The amount of scenarios, boards, and cards just in the basic game are enough to keep you entertained for a long time, and it practically begs you to make up your own. I played 3 games in various scenarios on different sides with different people and lost every single one. Never was I left feeling like the dice or cards had failed me. I was simply left seeing how I could do it better next time. In a game with so much randomness, it translates to pure fun. My rating could easily go down if I see the scenarios having a simple way for one side to always win, or it could go up if it continues to be this much fun. One caveat: this game is not for children. Too scary, mild innuendo, and a few swear words make this better suited for a teenage or older crowd.

RATING: 6.5
This one has everything Zombies!!! promised. Let me explain:

Zombies!!! has awesome miniatures, and tons of them. It has a board full of houses, and has you play a survivor trying desparately to outgun and outrun the slow-moving menacing evil clawy bity zombies.

But, the mechanics are sluggish, the cards are so situational that many of them become barely playable, things in general are unbalanced with some stuff being really powerful and other stuff being really weak.

LNoE on the other hand has balanced cards, great mechanics, plays easily without much downtime, and gives both the zombie player(s) and the survivors tons more options and things to do and stuff to manage.

Overall, a really great game, expanded by superb expansions to an incredible package.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
This is NOT the best zombie game by far. The best zombie game in my view is [b]Dead of Night[/b]. See my comment on the that game to find out why. (I haven't played Zombie Plague yet.)

Last Night on Earth is fun with a good group...but because of the group, not because of the game. The game itself is clunky, light and artificial. Since the events and player powers happen through card-play, they come out of nowhere. Plus there are player abilities that also come out of nowhere. Thus the elements of zombie films in this game are very "gamey": they are artificial devices to allow players to do certain things for internal game objectives, but they do not flow organically from the subject matter of zombie survival horror itself. This eliminates the claustrophobia, fear and tension that you find packed in real games like Dead of Night. In fact, I'd say DoN is both simpler (fewer rules) but deeper, more difficult, more tense, and far more immersive. LNOE by comparison is fast food: processed cheese on spam with ketchup all over. Popcorn with fake butter. It's a trans fat of a game.

RATING: 8
Initial rating 7. Further plays may raise this rating.

Update: Advanced rules moved this to an 8. Just wish I could find or make rules for the tractor... See, many components in the game have no rules associated with them; they are included for use in future and home brew scenarios. This is both cool and annoying (trying to locate rules which don't yet exist). The rule book has some substantial ambiguities, but these are overcome by player agreement before play begins. The rules also sometimes slide into truly tortured grammar and syntax -- as if translated from another language. Seems to have been designed in Washington state, so that's probably not the case though.

Depending on how Flying Frog supports this title, it could be a real winner! With additional scenarios springing up regularly, this seems likely.

The less said about the "Soundtrack" the better. I prefer Black Dice, Coil, God Speed You Black Emperor, Throbbing Gristle, John Zorn, Aklo, even Stravinsky over this upbeat, almost danceable CD.

Later: Bumped this up to a 9 after playing it all day long with friends, crafting one new homebrew scenario after another. Huge replayability right out of the box -- as much a game constructor kit as a game.

RATING: 9
This is a game for people who love zombies, like (and know how) to play cooperative (survivors, zombie hordes), and generally love to play out theme. 

The mechanics do a great job for this purpose, and the variety of missions and player combinations ensure great replayability. There is some noticeable draw luck involved, and not everyone likes that. Also, this is NOT a serious survival Zombie game (ATZ does a much better job at that). But there are a lot of tactical decisions to be made and coordination with other players is absolutely necessary.

LNoE is about the only Zombie game I can play with both kids and wife, everyone enjoys it, and it is one of the few games that is still being requested regularly after several years of play - the perfect game for dark and rainy nights for some good old Halloween Americana.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Very polished.  Much less errata than most card-based games.  Oozing with theme and fun.  Easy to for players to jump-in or drop-out mid-game (a rare quality).

Only reason it is not a 10 is the great amount of luck (cards, timing, dice-rolls) that can give one side a great advantage.  Not that I can think of a way to reduce these occasional imbalances without hurting the wonder replayability.

RATING: 6
A seemingly fun game that is just too random.  I honestly believe that it fails by making it competitive rather than coop.  Zombies get to draw cards every turn, move every turn, and move through walls, whereas the "heroes" must choose to either move or draw a card. Should combat ensue, the zombies win ties, but are only pushed back if they should lose to a similarly armed hero and are killed only on doubles (on two dice).  In short, a random shit-fest of lack-luster play.

RATING: 9
This is a fantastic recreation of your favorite B-Rate zombie movie in table-top game format.  All of the artwork is created using actual actors or models with heavy doses of photoshop to create the spooky atmosphere and film grain. The box comes with a collection of different scenarios each with different objectives and winning conditions for both the hero team and the zombie team.  They even included a collection of bits that aren't even used in the provided scenarios encouraging user created content, most of which can be found here on the 'Geek.  Game play is easy to learn, combat is resolved quickly, and almost every game yields an "Oh-Snap!" moment.

RATING: 6
My Brother bought this to play with family since it is light on rules and was hopefully big on fun. We were actually all pretty bored as there were no real decisions to make, very little so my biggest complaint but yes it is just a "hack and slash" game so it is what it is.  

I had heard a lot about the game and wanted to like it, I do like heavy on theme games big on fun but it just didnt come together for us.  Note that I am not a "Zombie" fan like many people are but I do have no problem playing a good light themed fun game if it has things going for it. 

Overall I think the game was very well produced and as far as an "Evil Dead" type board game goes, you would probably have a hard time doing better than this. Everything is there that you would want and they threw in a good bit of variety.  

All these types suffer from a couple of things which is some group dependancy and because it is semi-coop a dominant player can run the show a little too much, not really knocks on the game, just something to watch for with this type of game. 

I will have to replay it with a different group to hopefully bring it more to fruitation but at most will be a 7 for me. I do think its a good hack and slash kill the Zombie game, game time is good and luck not an issue for this, some more decisions would be what I would want different but I'm not sure how you would add them in, again it is what it is which for me is just much too simplistic in its raw form (and if the family didnt like it then I dont need to own it). Could make a good gateway game especially for Zombie fans.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
So I love this game, mostly because of its great theming and malleable mechanics.  

There are some games that I feel are not meant to be altered, but to me, Flying Frog created this game with every intention that the player would make tons of house rules and ultimately make it their own.

The game my friends and myself have put together with LNOE is sooooo much fun.  One of the biggest changes is that we took the heroes forced play order mechanic, and instead gave them 4 actions a turn (where they can only shoot once per turn). We also made an AI mechanic for the Zombies that (give or take a few cards) makes this game work pretty flawlessly as a pure coop.

I have played through just a handful of their scenarios and have created and played many.

I love all the parts that come with it and feel they are great quality.  This goes without mentioning all of the amazing expansions that really add so much depth to the game.

There is also an awesome community of player fans of this game that are always offering interesting alternate play styles and all kinds of content.

I have converted many Zombicide fans to LNOE fans and proudly so.  If you are creative and looking for an awesome Zombie game, get this one please.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
This game is one of my favorites. A game that lives up to the "survival-horror" genre, since it often ends with the survivors running for their lifes and leaving their friends behind in panic.

The game posseses a good replay value since the map consist of 8 big map tiles who all have diffrent houses, which contains diffrent abilities/objects that the survivors can use AND the map can be randomized 

one player takes on the role of the zombies and the other play like the survivors. The survivors goal is to survie through the scenario chosen, examples like finding gas and a pair of car keys to start up a car in order to escape or defending a manor.

RATING: 3.75
Last Night on Earth is a very thematically beautiful game. The components all look very good (save for the unpainted miniatures), and all of the elements of the game really wrap up to this nice, B-movie zombie package. All complete with a soundtrack that, in my opinion, really adds a lot to the experience.

...But the game takes 5 hours! For the amount of depth this game has (which is little, its mechanics are no better than American games from the '90s), I would enjoy it more if it took substantially less time. I feel like I'm making few meaningful choices, the luck runs the show, and while the journey is fun and flavorful, I walk away from the game feeling let down. I likely had no real impact on whether or not the game was won or lost, and due to its length, it's probably the only game we played that night.

RATING: 6.5
2011-10-15 

Initial Rating 9.0 (December 2010)

I love Zombie games so maybe (just maybe) I’m a little biased here folks ;).

For a time my favorite zombie game, now it is in my top 3 zombie games (after Mall of Horror and at the same level of Dead of Night), also it was in my top ten of games for a while. 

I think this is one (if not THE ONE) of the best zombie games ever made, I have to play more, but I really dig this game. It has superb components (except the soundtrack which is crap), engaging dynamics between heroes and zombies, super replayability due to new expansions and scenarios, it has a great theme (obviously), it plays well with 2, 3 or 4 players. It is also a fast paced game so you won’t get bored with it. 

Bottom line don´t expect a highly tactical or strategic  game, this is a fun game with lots of luck. LNOE is one of my favorite games.

Current Rating: 8.0
[hr]

2015-07-14

The first time I played LNOE was on 2010, that was also the year I took boardgaming as my main hobby, however, in these 5 years my gaming tastes have changed a lot (evolved?). I’m no longer the same person so, nowadays, I no longer enjoy LNOE as I used to. In fact I sold my copy of the game. Due to this, I’m downgrading its rating so it matches my current feelings for the game with the BGG recommended rating system.

I love that a player can control the zombies, this is still the only zombie game I have played who has this feature. I no longer enjoy the gratuitous luck inherent in the game. LNOE can take well over 2 hours so the high luck factor begins to bother me. All things considered,  I’m still rating it very highly because nostalgia plays a part too, had I know the game for the first time today, I suspect its rating would be much lower. As it stands, LNOE is almost a good game for me,  I will settle for playing it from time to time but I don’t need the urge to own it.

Ex Top Ten Game.

Current Rating: 6.5

RATING: 6
I wanted to like Last Night on Earth, but my first play really fell flat.  As in many "one v. many" games, the zombie player gets to do a lot more interesting things than the human players do, particularly when the zombie player gets a lose-turn card to play on a human.  I doubt I'll ever get to play the zombie master, so that's a huge problem for me.  

The basic (kill 15 zombies) scenario seems to hinge on whether the humans can find enough weaponry.  Which is fine, I suppose, but tends to break the game when the humans can't find any decent weapons.

I can't imagine wanting to play LNOE when I could play either the Buffy game or Wabbit Wampage instead.  The only thing Last Night on Earth has on either game is plastic zombies.

I'll try to play at least once more so as not to give up on the game too quickly.

Classic B-movie fun!

RATING: 6
This game has a problem. It absolutely MUST be dramatic and close to be of any interest, and the game has no mechanics to offset the randomness to ensure a decent play experience whenever you bring it out. Each play I could rate a 4 or a 9 or anywhere in-between depending entirely on card draws and die rolls. Our first game (Save the Townsfolk) was an absolute cakewalk for the Heroes because they happened to draw the townsfolk they needed early, the zombie player had lousy spawning rolls, and the whole game felt pointless. Now I recognize that subsequent games are likely to have a better dramatic arc, but since there's nothing in the game to help ensure that, the next game could end up being just as lousy. This game has some serious design holes and the rules are sloppily written. Still, I bet I would have some good experiences with it, I just can't predict when!

Cons:
- Seems a little long for what it is.

RATING: 4
Graphically, a well-made zombie game. The rules are simple, but the execution is [b]too simplistic[/b]. Feels like a [b]'tag-you're-it' or 'run-around-the-map'[/b] game. Many scenarios seem unintuitive and lack suspense. The Nurse Preacher combo is very broken, but the heroes don't stand a chance without it.

Seems very skewed towards the zombies. It takes too much effort to search for the card you want! By then, you're swarmed. Doesn't help that zombie cards hurt A LOT!

By the way, the CD was a nice idea, but the composed songs [b]lack eeriness and fullness[/b] (bass). At times, it gets amateurly midi'ish. I think the [b]sound is too dead[/b] (not zombie dead either); it needed some reverb.

This game proves that Flying Frog is purely art lure and minimal in gameplay. I am boycotting them because they think they can [b]win gamers with simple sex appeal[/b].
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
A well-produced zombie game with great components and simple gameplay. Its enjoyable and definitely one of the better zombie games I've played, but there are still some problems with it. Most importantly, the majority of gameplay centers around cards. And the cards are wordy. Lots of reading and re-reading and time spent trying to figure out how to resolve effects when multiple cards are played at the same time.

Games can drag on (especially on first-play) when players spend a lot of their turn reading the cards before moving, thus slowing the game for everyone. Also, the Zombie players do not really seem to have much active gameplay. A lot of the game focuses on the Heroes. The Zombie player seems to have been included just to move the zombies. Just move 1 square... thats it. 

The good points: great components, fantastic soundtrack (albeit a little short), simple to learn and play. I think that with the right group playing QUICKLY and not analysing every single move, this game can be really fun. As it is, it currently rates just above average for me.

RATING: 8.3
Several plays.

All games played well. 2nd game had an unexpected hero win (it looked for sure like the zombies had it in the bag). Zombies won third game "at the wire." It could have easily gone either way.

Very nice components. Wonderful relatively short playing time. Random set ups (board, cards, scenarios and the choice of picking or randomly selecting heroes in play) make for a varied play experience (even if using the same scenario things can develop quite differently from game to game). 

Manageable game (bookeeping; number of pieces and rules complexity).

Atmospheric. Captures thematic flavor very well.

Calls for some good tactical planning in adapting to changing circumstances. (i.e. It has just started raining heavily - Do I still make my way across town to the police station to grab a shotgun - from the discard pile - as I had planned? The rain will slow me down making it easier for the zombies to intercept me).

Several good laughs and surprises in each game. Billy is in the garage and wounded. Three zombies are confronting him. But Billy is right at the door and very fast, being a track star and all. He will simply run out the door of the garage and put some space between himself and the zombies. No problem! Go Billy go! Hey! What's this? The door won't open! "I am afraid Billy can't go through that door... see here... it's locked!" Billy soon joins the rest of the dead meat in the room.

"Hey, let's hide in the cornfield." (By the way, that strategy worked for the short term, but as more zombies converged on  the cornfield the plan fell apart).

All three examples  above are actual game experiences.

RATING: 9
The Good: Strong Theme. Multiple scenarios. Plays short (around 2 hours). Good components. The Zombies were real tough to beat (at least in my first game), and that is a good thing, as a challenging game will see more table time. Manages to do a fair job of telling a story as the game progresses. Lots of life-or-death dice rolling. I found it very easy to play solitaire.

The Bad: Light on strategy, but there are meaningful choices to be made. 

No Ugly: The card decks were stuck together REAL HARD, and it was a challenge to separate them. Many cards were damaged due to the melted laminate. This was listed as an ugly, but great customer service saved the day by sending me new decks !

RATING: 7
We didn't really enjoy [thing=35815][/thing], so we were a little wary of trying another Flying Frog game.  We definitely tilt towards the more Euro style of game, so these types of thematic games generally don't work for the two of us.  Still, I was intrigued by [thing=29368][/thing] since it seemed like the theme really came through in the game.  We ended up getting this in a trade and we gave it a try this Halloween.

The components are nice and thick cardboard and I didn't mind the graphic design.  We started with the [i]Escape in the Truck[/i] scenario, since it seemed to give a specific and thematic goal to the heroes.  I ended up playing the heroes, as it felt like it would be harder to juggle four different characters while she played the zombies.  Surprisingly, we enjoyed the game (well, I enjoyed it while she tolerated it, which was still a big step).  The biggest reason is that the theme really does come through, not just in the artwork and flavor text, but also in the gameplay itself.  In the Truck scenario, the heroes are frantically searching for the keys and a can of gas to get out of Dodge before the zombies eat them.  It seems to make sense and the mechanisms support the theme.  One of the problems with [thing=35815][/thing] is that it felt very abstract and arbitrary despite the thematic costuming---why am I randomly wondering around the countryside in circles?  Partly, I think this problem is attributable to the lack of a player that you're playing against.  The game feels like it lacks a soul.  Some cooperative games can get away with this type of abstract or puzzly feeling if the mechanisms behind the game are strong enough (such as in [thing=30549][/thing]), but this fails in a more complex and random random thematic game.  In contrast, in [thing=29368][/thing] you're playing directly against another human, so the choices that the zombies and humans make are much more tense.  

Still, the game is very random, so you have to be in the mood for that.  It's not really a complex strategy game.  With two players, one player will have to juggle four hero characters, which is not ideal.  Plus, I think these types of thematic games really need a group of people to really get the feel and excitement out.  We'll have to wait to bring this out with a larger group of people.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.8
What I like the most at this game is the fact that there are two different play styles which must be balanced. I find this difficult to achieve in any game (pc, board game etc). Also the fact that it is scenario based ads a lot of replayability because each player can come up any time with new scenarios more interesting then actual scenarios (although actual scenarios are very interesting). The only minus of the scenarios is the fact that the producers doesn't suggest players to try scenarios that players and zombies have a mission to do. For example in all scenarios players must do something and zombies must stop them. I would like from the producers to come with something like: players to something, zombies do something and each one have a choice to stop the other. Of course players can do a scenario like this but it should come as an example from the producers.

Overall the game is very fun specially when multiple players are involved in the game. Also I like the theme of the game and I think it works very good with the game-play.

What would have make the fight much more interesting is if the producers would have user special dices instead of normal D6 dices. Something like in Earth Reborn. I thing it would have made the fight much more dynamic.

Luck and randomness count in this game but not that much as some people say ... without right tactic players can't win even if luck is on their side. I believe if there neither of the two elements are not involved fun factor loses some points.

Another disadvantage of this game is 1v1 game because the hero player must play with four heroes. Its kinda hard to manage all the abilities and stuff of all four heroes. I did some plays in 1v1 with only 2 heroes, 7 zombies and 2 L shapes (instead of four) ad it plays quite nice ... so this is a workaround for those that find this problem irritating. 

I recommend this game because is very fun, has great theme, lot of replayability, players can customize game with new scenarios and also two different play stiles.

Advantages:
- very fun
- high player interaction
- two different play styles
- lot of replayability
- easy-medium to learn
- high quality package content

Disadvantages: 
- not a lot of strategy required
- luck can count a lot in some situations
- difficult for the hero player in 1v1 to play with 4 heroes
- some cards are not explained very well

RATING: 5
It’s simply the definitive zombie game. 

Though movement is still dice driven, character abilities and event cards create offsets to the detriments of the movement, and truly most of the flaws you might find here. I also enjoy that the game play is simple to the point that AP shouldn’t ever have a home, and that the turns are bite sized enough that the game moves along briskly. Further, since combat often occurs on both zombie and hero turns there always seems like something to do. The objectives also seem well balanced and impress a sense of urgency and tension heretofore unseen in other games of its ilk.

This one is already slated for our Halloween party, and it’s certain to see more than one play that day; certainly many more to come.

Update:

Years later and newer designs have made this virtually obsolete.

RATING: 10
I find that the kind of game that captivates me most these days are games where I become immersed in the setting and the game mechanics evoke the theme that they are trying to depict.

Some of my favorite games do this so well: Arkham Horror, Railroad Tycoon, Fury of Dracula, DOOM: The Boardgame, Dungeon Lords, and my absolute favorite of all, Man O'War. 

Add one more game to that list of immensly satisfying and entertaining games, because Last Night on Earth not only captures the feeling of a Zombie Apocalypse, it does it with simple mechanics and intuitive gameplay. LNoE also is unique in that the artwork for the game is done in a "B" movie style format and all the characters in the game are potrayed by actors and photographed as if they are in scenes from a movie.

This has the effect of creating a story as you play, one that is every bit as engaging as a zombie movie, yet significantly more enjoyable! 

Being the 1st game from Flying Frog Productions, you would think that there would be gaps in the productions or game play or design, yet that is not the case at all. LNoE plays with few referals to the rules, the things you do make sense from a game standpoint AND from a thematic standpoint and there are always new and unusual things that come up during a game.

Last Night on Earth is only made better with all the expansions and it has steadily risen in my ratings to become a game that I almost always want to play (time allowing) and one that I can see bringing many years of enjoyment down the road.

Lightweight gaming doesn't come much better than this.

RATING: 8
Reminiscent of playing M:tg with restricted cards. There are a lot of good, stock cards and some amazing "bombs" to continue the M:tg vernacular. 

In a nutshell the rules are fine with some notable exceptions. The development on the other hand, is not good. 

Random movement for heroes is irksome. I'd preffer the option to 'take 3' or roll (ala DnD 3rd edition)

The ammo/breakage rolls add an extra layer of chrome that may add to the theme or, dare I say, mood of the game. However it adds a superfluous rule that bogs down already slow game play. 

The game promises replayability with different character combinations and scenarios. Whether or not the game delivers remains to be seen.

Bumped to an 8 on 8-3-08

RATING: 7
I was originally under the impression that this was a purely cooperative game, but it's actually a team game, with a group of Heroes vs. a group of Zombies.  While I was initially concerned about that, I ended up greatly enjoying this game, as it feels extremely balanced between the two parties and has an amazingly engrossing theme.  The soundtrack provided isn't spectacular, but seriously, how many games have you played which come with their own music?  I feel like this game took the typical mindless zombie game and turned it into something with serious strategy, great replay value, and extremely fun gameplay.  Although it has recently been replaced by the superior Betrayal at House on the Hill, this is still a very fun large-group game, and I hope we get to play it more often.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Game in a Nutshell:  B-movie flavored scenarios pitting Team Zombies vs. Team Humans in a fight for survival or brains.

Played as: 3,4,6 player

Pros: The sense of theme and tension is immediatly apparent, trash-talking is abundant, and there's loads of high-tension dice rolls with groans or cheers to follow. I'm a big fan of how they presented the game which further drives home how the experience plays out like a campy horror flick. Loads of hilariousity. Just a smashing success in thematic story-telling game design. 

Cons: Sure, sound decision making is important, but if you're looking for strategic depth, you'll be left hungry. This also leads to boring down-time (little to plan or concentrate on) if played with people who can't keep the game moving. More balance in the scenarios would be nice.  

Other: I haven't been able to try playing as the Zombies yet but so far it seems that either side is equally enjoyable which isn't always true for asymetrical design. Also, I listened to the CD but haven't used it during the game... I didn't think it was as bad as people made it out to be.

Best Use: Great game for cutting loose and playing out a story.

RATING: 6
After many plays, I have a very strong opinion that this is an okay game with a great theme. It's not, unfortunately, the slam dunk I thought it might be.

I like the components. I like the look of the maps. I like the character art. I like the theme. I like the box art. I like the insert. I'm pretty sure I like this game for what it is--light, fun, brutal, easy to learn.

However, at least one of the scenarios is a total dog, some of the cards are odd (in a bad way), there are a few grey areas in the rules and there's something generally missing that I can't quite put my finger on. It pains me to give it a 6. But it is a 6.
