=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Trashy, enjoyable game. Rules are imbalanced, gameplay is not particularly deep, some scenarios are somewhat broken, but it doesn't matter in the slightest. This is not a well balanced, well designed game: this is a beer and pretzels game that oozes theme and plays out exactly like a zombie B-Movie, complete with all the clichés of typical zombie movies. That said, it's awesome. 

There are so many instances in this game that will make you laugh. That time the zombies ate player A and C while they were getting it on in the Police Station? Classic. That time the previously helpless priest saved the day (and won the game) by pushing zombies back with a fire extinguisher and blowing them up with dynamite? You'll remember that one fondly. No one cares if they win or lose, whether they were hopelessly outnumbered or the game was ridiculously unbalanced: it's all about the journey.

Only gripe is the elimination of players, making for bored people wishing they could get back into the game. I've fixed this with house rules: when killed humans always turn into zombie heroes which are played by the same player. To ensure they feel like they're contributing to the zombie team (they don't control a group of zombies, just the zombie hero), they're movement is still D6 and fight combat and wounds are identical to that of heroes (can still move through walls like other zombies). Quite literally a hero for the zombie team, who actively contributes in making things all the more difficult for a 25% smaller hero team. Heroes can no longer sit in a building and continually search while zombies slowly make their way forward, there is a faster, stronger creature ready to prey on the slow and foolhardy. That'll teach 'em for letting their friends die.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
One of my very favorite "story" board games - everyone I've introduced the game to loves it and it's usually the first thing my adult group will choose to play.

I've also played this game with the kids (ages 13-18) at the after-school game club I run and they LOVE it.

The important point with this game is that the story and the play experiences are much more important than who wins or loses - there's a high degree of luck involved in this game but that's what makes it so special and what makes those times when the heroes scratch out a victory so memorable.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
Played once with four people.  This is a co-op action game wherein players play either heroes or the zombies that are trying to eat the heroes.  Regardless of the number of players there are always 4 heroes and up to 14 zombies on the board, and one person always controls the zombies.  Heroes are underpowered at first, but can get items (cards) in buildings that give them better chances to fight off the zombies.  Fights are easy and quick to resolve, and the game overall felt very balanced.  For instance, heroes have a good chance of "fending off" zombies right from the start, but have trouble killing them without weapons; even when the heroes do get weapons, every time they're used they have a chance of breaking.  

The game has multiple scenarios that come with it, and I look forward to playing more of them.  I absolutely love that only one of the scenarios focuses on killing the zombies; all the rest focus on the heroes having to actually carry out some task (and it not mattering at all how many zombies they kill).  I also love that the game is co-op; this leads to lots of player interaction and lots of players helping players.

RATING: N/A

Our 2-player game was incredibly tense, the zombies destroyed the human team; due in part to lucking out with some good cards in the early game. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This one is all about the theme, but it somehow manages to capture that theme so perfectly. The game has this way of arranging moments that are almost cliched tropes of zombie horror films: the sherrif's son, because of his teen angst is turned into a zombie, and goes to eat his father. The father, too distraught to kill his own son is also turned into a zombie. The brave ex-military cook from the diner, stages a distraction so the farm girl and the priest can get away in the truck. And on and on.

The components are exquisite, the game play is surprisingly balanced, the box and the expansion come cram-packed with extras to encourage players to make their own little scenarios, etc.

Yes, it's schlocky, and there is not a lot of deep thinking or strategy involved. For instance, the main mechanic to move heroes around the board literally is roll-and-move. But somehow, none of that seems to matter. When you get in the middle of the game, you end of having so much fun that the light nature of the game is unimportant.

RATING: 7
A fun dice-rolling zombie game where one (or two) players are the zombies trying to kill the hero players.
Heroes are able to find weapons, items and event cards to help them survive the zombie onslaught.
I like the fact that the zombies are player controlled as this makes it more challenging for the hero players.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I keep changing my opinion of LNoE, at first I hated it and supported those who slagged it off, but the more I played it the more I liked it!

The game is still a little too swingy at times, but it's  a good zombie game with interesting scenarios and possibly the most fun playing as 'Overlord' as you'll ever get!

It also has manly, dangerous zombies that can be terribly tough to defeat and most of the time are better just avoiding (something which seems to be rare in the recent flood of zombie games).

However, the expansion Growing Hunger is essential in several ways and improves the game ten-fold!

I'd rate it as low as 6/10 on it's own, but at least 8/10 with Growing Hunger included, the expansion really is that good!

As with A Touch of Evil be careful of the number of expansions you invest in though, as it will bloat the game to unplayability.

Progressive Rating: 5-4-5-6-8-7.

RATING: 7
This will be the game I break out every October.  LNOE is a simple yet addictive game that drips with theme and provides a good narrative; clearly a labor of love. Yes, it's a dicefest, but that's ameritrash, baby!  There is some luck, but good strategy, player cooperation, and card management usually carries the day, err...night.  

I like the use of photography and models for the characters as it adds to the whole 'B' movie vibe and makes the characters more "real."  (The hero profiles at the end of the rulebook are a nice touch). My one minor quibble is that the map art could have been better.  The "town center" is only a grassy field with an old well when it could have depicted a park with a gazeebo, fountain, etc.  Also, I would have liked the town area to have concrete instead of grass connecting the buildings. The CD is a nice, but unnecessary, touch. I was hoping for Bauhaus-like music and fearing a bad 70's porn soundtrack, but it's neither.  It sounds like atmospheric new age music (and well done at that).  Overall, LNOE is a great game and I look forward to the expansions (please give me an urban environment!).

RATING: 6
Played this for the first time at GenCon '08 and had a blast.  I think it was the burn it to the ground scenario.  Lately, I've managed to play it a few times with my daughters, 10 and 14, and it has gone over surprisingly well.  Helped that the first game was suitably dramatic.  We played "Escape in the Truck."  Jenny the farm girl was dusting zombies left and right, and Johnny had managed to fill up the truck with gas.  Problem was, while everyone was looking for keys, the zombie hordes converged on the truck in a swarming mass.  At the last minute they were blown to bits with some dynamite, and the heroes just barely managed to run to the truck, start 'er up, and take off.

Anyway, like as with Buffy, my 14 y.o. likes the action, and it's nice to see her and her sis cooperate and applaud each other's rolls.  The game is listed as 12+, but the mechanics are simple enough for my 10 y.o. to grasp.  Played for some goofy fun, it's a solid game.

My main criticism is that there are just too many cards.  I get a little tired of games that overutilize cards, and this game has its share of players digging through their cards because they can't remember what effects they've got that might be useful.  This also makes it a hard game to introduce to casual gamers.

Edit'14:  I still enjoy the game, for what it is.  At its best, it is a cinematic drama, and it's more fun when players are laughing over the in-game tropes.  The game is sooo swingy, though, in experience.  What cards come up when completely determines the experience of a scenario.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
In this zombie themed game, one (or two) players are the zombies, and the rest are heroes running around town. As players, roll the dice and move. There are strategic objectives one tries to achieve, such as killing 15 zombies, or rescuing four townsfolk.

It's a fun thematic game, that comes with a CD for music. It is heavily luck dependent and it is more of an experience game. There is lots of favour, and as the players, there is a ton of tension as the zombies close in on you. Just don't try to play this game too strategically.

RATING: 7
Some clever things here, but seems to be very crowd-specific.  I may have to re-rate this when I play it with a group of players more in tune with the theme.

---update---
As suspected, the group makes a huge difference.  It's also important to recognize that this is an experience game - if you go in with the goal of winning, you're doing it wrong.  This is about having some heavily themed fun first and foremost.  Luck can dominate a playing, but fortunately play time is short enough that it shouldn't overstay its welcome.  I'm keeping my initial rating of 6, but the fun value with the right people in the right mindset can bring the experience up a couple points.

RATING: 7
First impression (3 players): Thematic zombie-game where one player takes zombies and others control 4 humans trying to do a mission in zombie infestated little town. The game was better than I had thought as it wasn't too fluffy and actually base gameplay is very simple. There are quite powerful action cards for both humans and zombies that probably aren't all that balanced but here it doesn't matter that much as game is more about theme and having fun than serious gaming. Battles are fought with dice and for humans without weapons it is very hard to kill a zombie as you need to roll a higher pair (with 2 dice without bonuses) than zombie rolls with his 1 die. So having luck with dice helps too but my first character in first game died straight away after rolling 5-5 and 6-6... The pressure of zombies seems to be constantly (just) overwhelming (enough) which is a big part of game having just right tension.

Overall it is a good game, it might be slightly too long to be played too often for what it gives but if can be played in a right type of group it is a blast every now and then.

RATING: 7
I wanted to own one true Ameritrash game and bought this one. The gameplay might suck a bit (roll and move for example) as I expected (it does in most Ameritrash games) but I do enjoy the theme and components. There is little room for strategies and tactics in this game as luck dominates pretty much everything. However, there are some issues you need to keep in mind when playing either heroes or zombies. After few plays the game seems to be easier for the zombie player but I do not mind that as it kind of suits the theme. All in all Last Night on Earth is not a great game but with the right group and after drinking few beers it can be fun.

RATING: 5.2
As far as zombie games go, it's one of the best.  That being said, this theme is still wide open and looking for its one true leader.  LNOE makes a valiant attempt to be that *one* definitive game, but sadly it falls short.

The "roll to move" mechanism is rather weak, as are the large spaces in the center board.  

All in all, if you like zombie games, you'll probably enjoy LNOE.  If you don't care for the theme very much, then don't purchase the game as there's plenty of sacrifices in the design in order to "make" it a zombie game.

RATING: 8.15
The perfect Zombie experience! Nice...roll-playing with the zombies! When I bring this game out, my first impression is how much it really seems like a great grade B horror movie! RATING: 6
Some games are only as good as the game group you play them with and LNOE is one of those. The rules are simple and the gameplay repetitive; the art-work is deliberately shonky and the theme hokey so you really need players to be chucking themselves into it - making the zombie noises, role-playing the heroes etc. otherwise it will be dull. Unfortunately I have yet to find a game group who have fallen for LNOE's dubious charms so it has always been just a bit rubbish.

I should say that the components are really good. Not so much the mini's which are of the the soft, rubbery variety but the board bits, tokens and cards are really thick and glossy and tactile. The drawn art is also really cool and the game looks awesome when all set up. 

In summary if you have the right sort of group this game would be a riot; although you could probably say the same about Monopoly.

RATING: 8
Muy buen juego. Las partidas son rápidas y divertidas, hay poco tiempo de espera entre jugadores y es altamente rejugable. Las cartas y los diferentes personajes dan mucha variedad y hacen que cada partida sea diferente, aunque se esté jugando el mismo escenario. El ambiente de peli de zombis de serie B está MUY logrado y la mecánica del juego es muy narrativa. A poco que se le eche imaginación, se producen situaciones muy cinemáticas, escenas que bien podrían formar parte de esas pelis. La calidad de los componentes es brutal. Las cartas están ilustradas con fotos de actores que representan personajes, zombis y los eventos que describe cada carta.

En este juego se pueden matar muchos zombis, pero no son para nada fáciles de matar sin las armas y el equipo adecuado... y uno corre el peligro de que le mate un zombi y pasar a formar parte de la horda como un zombi mucho más poderoso. 

La única pega (y por eso no le doy más nota) es que a veces una buena mano de cartas de salida condiciona mucho la partida y puede decantarla muy pronto hacia un bando. Pero esto no suele ocurrir y, si pasa, siempre se puede montar otra partida en poco tiempo.

Muy recomendable.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Prendi tutti i film di Romero e segnati temi, luoghi, personaggi e situazioni. La tranquilla provincia americana? C'è. La procace figlia del fattore, il prete, il vicesceriffo e il vagabondo? Ci sono. Case in cui barricarsi, o pickup da riempire di benzina per fuggire? Eccoli. Valanghe di zombi che escono da ogni dove? Quanti ne vuoi. Sono tutti in Last Night on Earth.
Il gioco è pesantemente calato nell'ambientazione, e tutto è in tema: l'eccezionale veste grafica (non disegni ma fotografie: i personaggi sono attori reali), gli scenari, le citazioni presenti sulle carte azione, i componenti (il counter dei turni per primo).
Le meccaniche sono semplicissime, il gioco è di breve durata e ti consente di concedere la rivincita nella stessa serata. E' inoltre corredato da segnalini "superflui", che permettono ai più volenterosi di creare (o scaricare, sia dal sito ufficiale che da mille siti apocrifi) mini-scenari una volta che quelli presenti, un po' pochini, sono stati affrontati fino alla nausea.
Sembra un commento da 8, vero? Purtroppo non basta il mio amore per il genere zombie e la bella confezione, il gioco è pessimo. Benché filologicamente giusto che ci sia uno sbilanciamento di forze a favore degli zombi (nei film vincono sempre), nel gioco questo ammazza la tensione: da una parte gli zombi che pescano e giocano carte azione in continuazione, dall'altra gli eroi che devono sputare sangue per avere anche solo un oggetto. Il giocatore-eroe gioca con frustrazione, impossibilitato dal troppo peso dell'alea su ogni aspetto del gioco a tentare una qualsiasi strategia; il giocatore-zombi non si diverte a sparare sulla croce rossa. Gli scenari sono molto impegnativi per i giocatori (la macchinosità del passaggio degli oggetti, fondamentale in molti scenari, rende tutto più difficile e segna l'esito della partita già dopo pochi turni) e, eccettuato forse lo scenario Defend the Manorhouse che lascia flebili speranze, quasi sempre letali.
Last night on Earth è uno dei giochi che ho atteso di più nel 2007, e allo stesso tempo una delle più grandi delusioni. Roba da rivalutare il semplice, spensierato e più bilanciato Zombies. Ma non è che gli zombi e i giochi da tavolo mal si sposano?

RATING: 4
This kind of game is fun to play on a turn-by-turn basis, but is so full of (1) die rolls and (2) card play that it requires a truckload of rules lawyering.  I also have the feeling (based on one play) that the system, built for countless (or at least dozens of) scenarios, isn't truly balanced for any of them.  

What I mean is that it feels like 80% of the time, the zombies have an easy (and inevitable) time of it, and 15% of the time the heroes have an easy (and inevitable) time of it, but you truly only have a knife-edge "who's going to win this game?" feeling 5% of the time (like "Betrayal at House on the Hill").  And games like this, though I want to enjoy them, always have me pretty worked up by the frustration of relying on constant dice rolls where you keep needing to beat the odds.

Ultimately, I just think there are better options out there for apocalyptic monster-fighting or zombie-fighting games (Arkham, Mall of Horror, Zombiecide, and even Betrayal would make my list before this one).

RATING: 7.5
All components look good and are of great quality. Cards, die rolls, equipment and missions can make the game tilt one side or the other pretty fast - which accentuates the stress of survival during the entire play, nothing is certain until the end. This is both great and sometimes annoying depending which side you are on, but at least players rarely feel that they are playing a losing game for too long. A couple of lucky searches can have all heroes armed and strong in fights. A couple of unlucky rolls can break all weapons and get a hero killed quickly. Some missions are definitely intended to be more of a challenge for the heroes (Search missions require luck on the cards picked up and the mansion defense is a desperate situation that requires lots of luck to win). This is bar none the best zombie survival game out there. I will purchase an expansion or two.

UPDATE#2
I really like this game. This game carries its theme very well,anybody with a passing knowledge of zombies and B movies will recognise the familiar tropes and archetypes involved, from the  very subtle too the downright obvious and the mechanics reflect the theme perfectly. It also plays very fast, although the optimum set-up would probably be with one zombie player. There isn't much downtime either, players can take there turns fast and if not playing there watching the zombies moving in. Large player groups seem to have the benefit of additional event cards which are powerful in knocking out the zombie cards.If you like AT games then this probably one of the best.
UPDATE#3 Im cooling down on this quite a bit and wondering if there are better zed games out there.Might end up on the trade list!

RATING: 5
It's a neat flavorful game, but the mechanics are a bit off.  The zombies have a huge statistical dice advantage over the heroes, and are able to more effectively and more often use debuffs and penalty cards.  The searching instead of moving action makes thematic sense, but disallows the heroes from doing much of anything if they get a bad draw in the face of an advancing horde.  

I'd say a good fix would be a separate events deck for the heroes to draw from for free every turn, while still requiring them to search for items and weapons.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
[color=#CC0000]

    Update -- Please note that what is written below applies to the base game only.  I have no experience with the expansions which should add to the play experience.

    Players walked away from the board mid-game.  Vast degree of player disenfranchisement.

    Game sessions likely very lopsided in favor of one side or the other -- initial setup often predetermines the end result prior to turn one.  I appreciate this isn't billed as a stunner for deep play, but I'd like to have some level of say in the outcome.

    Some scenarios simply provide no options, turn after turn.  Players can get in situations where they are completely out of control of their character, there being exactly one obvious decision that often has no impact on the game turn after turn.  At times a fast-forward button would do this game a lot of good.  Standing in an empty building and using the "search" option turn after turn hoping for a character or a set of keys to turn up is just not sufficient to make people want to stay.

    No emotional investment in the character means roleplay aspect of the game is heavily hamstrung.  The characters can "find" things to defend themselves which in theory means an evolving character story, but they are generally lost or broken in short order so, again, there is no desire to emotionally invest in the state of the character as it changes.  You're as likely to be back to your starting condition at game end as you are anywhere else.

    Crowbars break in this game.  You ever try to break a crowbar?  For a game that depends on suspension of disbelief this kind of detail is very damaging.  Text and simple rule changes could close some pretty absurd conditions in the game.

    Any goal you achieve can be reversed at the turn of a card, and that can happen immediately after you've achieved the goal.  The opposing player may have the card in hand and be specifically waiting for you to achieve that goal so he can reverse it ON YOUR TURN.  Players get pissed off at that kind of thing.  We had two games (out of about five) where we simply stopped playing because the game had fallen into a degenerated state of play -- one side was totally dominating the other and there were simply no options to make a change.  You're not supposed to concede wins in multi-player games, but that proved useful for us.

    Movement rules can at best be described as "stunted."

    Combat rules a shade worse than the movement rules.  They're simple and that's nice, but simple needs to have some reasonable basis in reality.  I think it can be improved here.

    Designer goes on about play-testing it for eight years, but it is very apparent that games with similar mechanics and concepts never appeared on his table.  Vastly better games in this vein ([b]Buffy the Vampire Slayer[/b] comes to mind) make LNoE at best "obsolete" and likely make "broken" a far more sticky adjective.    I won't go that far, but I have absolutely no desire to return to this one.  There's a foundation here that can be made to work, but there are too many ways for the game to fall into a state where the game plays itself, leaving the players on the outside looking in.

    I very VERY much wanted to like this game, likely a factor in my level of disappointment.

[/color]

RATING: 2
There are two mechanics which absolutely blow this game for me:

* You spend your entire turn to draw a Hero card. Woo. Excitement. As much fun as skipping your turn or losing one. Except that, since many cards can be played on other Heroes, a strategy is for one player to run around the board, and the other players to play Hero cards to keep him alive.

On top of this, the buildings are barely thematic. You need to be in a building to draw a card, but which building doesn't matter. Yes, you can draw a specific object from a certain building, but only if it's in the discard pile. I'm not sure of the opportunity cost of running to another building for a specific object versus using this time to draw cards during your turns.

* Heroes roll two dice and pick the better of the two, but can't kill a zombie unless they roll doubles. Thematically, this is a perfect mechanic. The humans are quicker and more agile than zombies, but zombies are tough to kill. But, in gameplay, this becomes a tedious piece of accounting. Roll the dice, compare them, and do nothing. Fascinating!

I'll try out another zombie game before playing another game of LNoE, thanks.

Also: The mini's are notorious for being tacky when primed. Use either Super Clean (wear gloves) or Simple Green to remove the primer.

RATING: 8.5
To say the central mechanic of this game is to move and shoot is to over simplify the game.  Last Night on Earth does an excellent job of portraying every zombie movie in a board game.  The players decide who will play the heroes and who will play the zombies.  Each scenario has its own win conditions.  At the start of the game the zombies clearly have the upper hand, as most heroes start the game unarmed and have a difficult time actually killing a zombie.

Players are deciding where to move, what to do, and how not to get killed.  Most scenarios have a clock, and will end in a given number of turns, meaning each turn the heroes are pressured to do something that will count, so cowering in the corner isn't the best option, but neither is facing a zombie horde with no weapons.  This game plays equally well as a lite role playing game or as a pure strategy game.

RATING: 7
Set up the randomly generated town board, draw some random Hero characters and pick a Zombie player. Draw one of several scenarios and let the fun begin! This action game with RPG elements sees the Hero players frantically search through buildings to find weapons with which to defend themselves and scenario-specific items, whilst the Zombie player seeks to cut them off and take them down with special cards. The cards are all high quality and glossy, and feature real human actors. The game even includes a CD containing atmospheric music to really set the scene! The rules are very easy to master.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The small town of Woodinvale has been beset by a horde of zombies! (If fourteen constitutes a horde.) People have called this game "cooperative," but it's also a team-based game: 1-2 zombie players (splitting 14 zombies) compete against 1-4 hero players (splitting 4 heroes). Hero players really must work together to win. Five scenarios are included, each one with different victory conditions, but in general the teams try to kill each other. Zombies draw up to four event cards per turn, whereas heroes have to struggle and search buildings to replenish their event cards, items, and weapons. New zombies may re/spawn each turn (spawns are most likely when the horde is smaller) but a zombie event card can cause surprises. The map is composed randomly using a center piece and four out of six corner pieces with buildings on them. There are eight heroes to choose four from (also random unless all players agree). Zombies are slow, but on the zombie turn they ALL move one space. Heroes move 1d6 squares or stay still and heal (for young heroes) or search (when in a building). Hero movement is always stopped by running into a zombie. Zombies may move freely unless they're next to a human, and then the smell of brains is just too strong for them. Hero weapons may help melee combat, or may be used to fire at a zombie at a distance. The game comes with a lot of dice but they're handled very well and lead to exciting streaks of luck. ("Why! Won't! You! Die!") The "advanced" rules have a mechanic for preventing player elimination which works really well, allowing them to take a new character and compensating the zombies with an uber undead called a zombie hero. Since all games are fought against a sun clock, games end in a timely manner. The whole game is very cinematic and tense. I like it a lot. 8.5.

UPDATE 28-Nov-2010: Dropping to an 8, where it may not stay. Obviously, my desperate love of all things zombie has colored my initial opinion here. There is a distinct lack of barricading and hiding as the undead break effortlessly through walls to find you. The outcome of the game is very dependent on the luck of the cards, and while this gives the heroes an appropriate level of desperation, it doesn't often feel that surviving these challenges is due to the diligence of the hero players. On the other hand, as the zombie player, you are offered a delicious array of horrors and disappointments to bring down upon the heroes while they blind draw card after card waiting for the scenario items to come up. Score could drop, we'll see, especially if I manage to get another (better) zombie game to the table.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8.9
This game is enjoyable to say the very least. 

Production quality is god-like, I don't think I've seen another game that comes with MUSIC. WHAT!? Great detail and quality to the cards, and the dedication to actually cosplay for EVERY one!? Wow.

Game mechanics is pretty fresh and interesting, providing tactical depth, randomization and scenarios for gameplay variants, and nothing that seemed too strong or too weak.

The only reason it loses 1.1 points is because despite what I said, something about this game just isn't "jaw-breakingly fun." I don't feel invested in my victory other than hey, I want to win and make the other person lose. I don't feel attached to any of the characters, and it's essentially a "quick-match" arena style gameplay on videogames. Also, no zombie variants.

This review is based off of the core set.

RATING: 7.5
Very thematic experience game.  Certainly the best runnin' around killing zombie games out there (I think Mall of Horror is a much better game but it isn't really about running around and killing zombies).  There seems to be enough variety in the scenarios that you could get quite a few healthy plays out of this before it gets old.

I wish that there was a bit more encouragement for movement and objectives, but I've only played the basic scenario.  It made more sense to stay in one spot and search the same place every turn and let the zombies come to me.  (of course, knowing that the zombie player should have never had them approach, but is that against the spirit of the game).

The one thing that I didn't like about the game was that certain items can only become available in their appropriate buildings after a random draw reveals them and they are discarded.  It seems to me that they should be available to be searched for at the beginning.

This is a much improved version of Frag, which may sound like damning praise, but certainly lets you know what you are in for.

All in all, good fun.

RATING: 8
[rating lowered from 9.5 to 8] - Just to reflect the shiny & new effect.  Still a really fun game that I constantly want to play, but multiple 6-player games have demonstrated to me that the game can drag towards the end.I never expected to buy this game.  Zombies are not my thing.  However, I noticed a TON of LNOE pictures on BGG, and started looking through them.  "Hey, this looks like a lot of fun.", I thought.  For me, it all comes down to the approach.  The way that Flying Frog approaches the theme is exactly my style.  It's not serious and it's not silly.  It walks a narrow, campy line that allows for the evocation of equal amounts of horror and humor.  I don't think I've ever really seen a complete zombie movie, but this game is an exact representation of how I think it would be.  The characters are fantastic, and the card names and effects are just perfect.However, there are a few considerations:1) Quality of game materials can be spotty.  Everything is ultra glossy, which may or may not be to your liking.  Personal I *don't* like it, but the game is so good, it doesn't matter much to me.  Another guy in my game group thinks the materials are fantastic and of amazing quality.2) The CD Soundtrack is, unfortunately, a play-once-and-put-it-away sort of thing.  Most of the soundtrack to "Pirates of the Caribbean" is a FAR better choice if you want atmospheric music.3) The company seems committed to the game.  They have released an official scenario online and there is an expansion in the works.  They also appear to be extremely friendly and have a strong presence on BGG.4) The rulebook contains a hidden sentence near the copyright that says "The Martians are coming!".  There is speculation that this could mean the release of a re-themed Mars Attacks version of the game.  Sounds AWESOME to me.5) Dice play an important role in this game.  So far, my experience has been that the Heroes have almost NO CHANCE to win the game against the Zombies.  Other players experience just the opposite.  I can only take this to mean that the dice (and card draws) have a significant ability to determine the balance of power.  Is this bad?  No, not in a game like this.  It will play differently time and again.6) The Rulebook is very nicely done.  And the rules themselves are really great.  Just enough to get the game running nicely, with nothing overly complicated.  Even so, you *will* need to refer to a FAQ now and then because the rules, though clearly written, are susceptible to gamer over-analysis which could lead to confusion.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7

( The names of some of the song tracks are hilarious and fit right into the events going on in the game.) At the same time, for me, the game was getting tense as it drew closer to a finish.

I'll play it safe and rate it right in the middle, a 7.  I'll have to give this a few more plays to see if has any table-staying power.

RATING: 9
Me and my group of survivors are totally addicted to this game. If people tell you there is no strategy in this, don't believe them. If you don't have a plan, you will die. If the zombies don't have a plan, they'll die (a second time). Of course luck is an important factor as well, but in my eyes it only simulates real life (after a zombie apocalypse), the best plan can go terribly wrong. 

Buy this and you will play a movie. There will be triumph, there will tragedy, there will be lots of funny moments. Never split up, don't get emotionally attached to other survivors and always remember: This could be your last night on earth.

I'm giving this only 9 points because of the promblems some people had while painting these great sculpted miniatures.

It's more like just managing the game for the survivor players.  I love the theme and playing as the survivors is more fun and interesting but somebody has to get the booby prize of playing the zombies.

RATING: 7.5
Even though it involves that much dice rolling (not a big dice fan) I really enjoy this. Naturally, I love the theme but additionally I like that you can play in "teams" against each other, one side Zombies, the other side heroes.
The rules were a bit confusing on some things, LNoE is a light, fun game but it took us a bit to get everything sorted out which is weird for a game that is fairly simple in its mechanics. Nevertheless, to me this is fun in a box. Thematic details where chance decides whether the heroes pitchfork breaks or the shot you fired hit the Zombie deadly round the movie-like experience, the soundtrack the game comes with is a neat bonus that I appreciate. We played with 4 (2 hero players, 2 Zombie players) which worked very well, need to see how other combinations play out.
If you want strategy, clearly look somewhere else, but if you want to fight or be a Zombie, look no further. Looking forward to trying more of the scenarios, great game for Halloween!
Now played two player (one zombie, one heroes) and had a lot of fun but some of the rules are just very confusing and we still wing a couple of things.

RATING: 5
In a nutshell, this game seemed to me to be all about card play and not much about board gaming.  For the heroes, it was all about drawing the right cards at the right time, and for the zombies (who seem to have quite a challenge on their hands), it was all about trying to foil the heroes' plans by playing as many cards as possible.  For me, it certainly wasn't the most exciting experience around.  However, in its favour, I can say that it's not too difficult a game to learn and new gamers we have played it with have loved it.  And the production value is absolutely top-notch, with big, thick, cardboard components and very fun photographic artwork that really helps develop the individual characters.  The card text was a bit tiny for my aging eyes, but everything else looked great.  I also enjoyed the team play aspect of it, where 2 zombie players could team up against 4 human players.  But ultimately, for my zombie fix, I'll stick with the great "print and play" game, Zombie Plague.  Game design: 3.5/5  Personal enjoyment: 1.5/5  Total: 5/10

RATING: 7
Crud.  I like it.  Highly random; not much deep strategy, but clever card plays can have dramatic (and often amusing/exciting) impact.  Lots of fun with the right sort of group.  Even one person who isn't 'into' the game can really drag down a session.  Also suffers from too much cooperation; its easy for more experienced players to wind up 'playing for' the inexperienced ones.  Not an uncommon problem with team games.  While it does tend to favor the heroes, we've had a pretty good mix of games going both ways, and its often exciting and tense down to the last turn.

Painted: all heroes, 0 zombies
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is really a great zombie game.  I've just never found people who really want to play it.

If you like zombies, this is a sure thing.  The game play is fun and fast and the game is easy to teach.  You can have new players up and running in no time.

The important thing to remember here is that this is a game where the experience matters far more than who wins or loses.  They call that "Ameritrash" around these parts.

********************EDIT 01/06/2011**********************

I finally got to play this game with a group of people who were all about having fun.  We had some great moments that I'll remember forever.  A total blast.  Sure, we got crushed as the heroes, but I think everyone had a great time.

I've upped my rating to 7/10.  It was at a 4 before, but I think I let bad experiences mar my rating.

Es fácil de preparar y de aprender, con acción trepidante, como una película de Terror. Las posibilidades de cada bando estan al 50%. Túl hosszú az előkészület ahhoz, hogy megerősödjön a karaktered zombimészárláshoz (pl 10 körig bányászni egyhelyben a 17-ből... és ezen kívül SEMMIT nem csinálsz a köreidben), majd túl könnyen elveszted ezeket a fegyvereket (lelősz egy zombit és máris kifogyott a lőszer, a következőn eltört egyszerre a pajszer meg a baseball ütő). Nem tetszett hogy egy iskolás csaj ugyanolyan jól lő a revolverrel mint a sheriff. Egy helyben ácsorogva 4 játékos 10 körig ugyanabban a házban, ugyanazt a helyet kotorva talál minden szart, ez kivet a játékból. 2 házzal alrébbról fullra gyógyítani a zombi körében egy túlélőt megint mi már (varázslat?). Ha egyetlen overlord van túl erős, a találat vagy túlélő közelharc győzelem esetén újradobatás szintén, van összesen 1/3-ad esélyem lelőni a zombit, majd hogy kétszer egymás után megdobjam ezt az értéket 1/9-hez ami túl karcsú és rögtön veszítek abból a minimális életemből. Az hogy közelről leöljem a zombit közelít a lehetetlenhez (két kockából duplát ÉS nagyobbat mint amit ő dobott, 3 vagy 4 kockából is elég nehéz, ráadásul akkor több mint a fél játékot kotorászással töltöm). Közelharcban 10* legyőzhetem a zombit akkor se döglik meg, ő legyőz 2* és meg is haltam. 
Adok egy kegyelem kettest, mert vannak benne minik...

RATING: 8
I love this game. I think it captures the zombie B-movie theme so well, while having mechanics that work. Even the randomness (of the die rolls, of the cards drawn) adds to the theme - because when you're in a zombie movie, you never know when you'll get a lucky break, or when the zombies are just round the corner, waiting to mob you. Contrary to most people's opinion (so it seems), I love the soundtrack. It's just so cheesily bad and really goes with the whole B-movie theme. I find myself humming it in work, which is always a bad sign.

I also like the fact that it lets me be really immature: the LNOE card gets lots of nudges and winks and quotes from the card ("Gimme some sugar, baby.") in a creepy voice; playing as the zombies affords the opportunity to make ridiculous groaning noises and yelling "NOM NOM NOM!" when a hero gets eaten; and, for some reason, the phrase "Small Town Lawman" gets lots of giggles. I also like shouting, "Take that, you zombie-bastard!" with unnecessary gusto when one of my heroes *finally* takes a zombie out. 

I really enjoy playing this game, especially with the player interaction. It's such a good laugh, whether sober or drunk!

We hammered it over the Christmas period (to the point of playing five games on Christmas Day), so I think we're going to ease off it for now, in case I end up with another Carcassonne-situation on my hands.

RATING: 7
12/31/2010 - First-play impression: I wasn't quite ready for this one. I should have done a bit more research before taking it out and trying to teach it. Thus, our first play was a bit bogged down looking up rules, trying to read and discover why things seemed unbalanced, etc. We were making some critical mistakes until well into the game. 7/10/2013 - Well 2.5 years later from my first note above, I've played it now with proper preparation and the right group. It was good fun. I'm bumping my rating up from a 6.5 to a solid 7. Who knows, maybe it will climb with even more plays. If the scenarios add replayability, that will definitely help. I'm pleased to have it.

RATING: 6
Still trying to decide on my rating after a couple of plays.  It's probably between a 6 and a 7 at this point, which is disappointing as I was expecting more.  It is a good game as a whole, but is limited in a number of ways:  1) the zombie player is, well, a zombie.  Not many real decisions to be made playing that side;  2) there is a lot of text on the cards, which slows down what is best as a quick, theme-filled game;  3) some of the heroes (and some combinations of heroes) are much stronger than others; and 4) the ranged weapons (especially the shotgun) can make or break the game for the heroes as they are VERY powerful.  On the other hand, the game oozes theme and has a well-balanced hand-to-hand combat system that fits the theme well (zombies are reasonably easy to fend off but hard to kill without a weapon).  The randomness doesn't really bother me as it fits the theme and, anyway, the world would be a boring place if we only had perfect-information no-luck games to play.  Maybe some more plays, possibly with different number of players, will help me appreciate this more but based on the number of other games I'd rather play, I can't see this higher than a 6 or at best 7.

RATING: 7
I'm going for a solid, solid 8 for this and if it weren't for my recent decision to remove half markers would add a .5 to it but it's not exactly a 9 so 8 it's gotta be.  Officially going to state the best zombie game I've played taking this coveted spot from Mall of Horror.  A smooth running system that is co-op between the teams.  Theme is very dramatically implemented and generates the "in a horror movie" feel very well.  

So is this game filled with luck? YES! Dice and cards come on people it's as simple as that.  Don't like luck you aren't going to like this but let's face some facts here.  If a Zombie plague were to set siege to your town wouldn't surviving it be luck filled too? How man whacks in the head would it take with a meat cleaver to actually damage the brain of your next door neighbor-turned-zombie-friend to best them?  Is that the same number of whacks it'd take to the cranium of big buff pool guy-turned-zombie in your back yard? One....twhoooooo...three...SPALT! The world may never know. 

This game is a lite fare and should be approached and appreciated for that.

Lemme get it out there....I love this game.

RATING: 9
PROS: •Fun game, very thematic, unique, easy to learn. Movement system is cool, combat system as well; •The game unfolds itself without drifting away from the theme, even the cards have effects that thematically fit their titles; •Great artwork using photographs and filters;  •Gameplay is fine from 2 to several players, and the different characters and scenarios add great replay value to the game, intensified through the expansions. 

CONS: •The scenarios and player charts could be thinner and the miniatures could be made from a less limp material; •Some scenarios require a little bit of deck building beforehand, as some specific items must be dug from the deck and it can get really frustrating (the more cards you have, the worse it gets).

RATING: 5.75
I love the different scenarios, and the distinct abilities that each character has. Intelligent opponents are always a good thing, but random movement is something with which I take issue, and should be dependent (fixed) on the character, rather than a roll of the die. When I criticize games like this, my friends are quick to point out BattleTech; while attacking in BattleTech is determined by dice, terrain modifiers, movement, and damage have fixed values.

Games that have strategic elements, but rely so heavily on dice completely defeat the purpose of planning. If I wanted that much chaos, I'd play Yahtzee.

RATING: 6
Theme-driven good time.  Almost like a dungeoncrawler with zombies instead of orcs, goblins, and the other usual fantasy baddies.  The feel of a zombie movie comes across really well through both photography and graphic design.  The fact that the protagonists are so generic somehow heightens the experience, making the game even more about the zombies, and less about the heroes.  Several scenarios in the box, all of which are interesting.  For anybody who is scared away by luck, or doesn't play games for theme, do yourself a favor and stay away from this game.  The fortune of the heroes is extremely dependent on what they find in the deck, which means that there's lots of great suspense and a feeling of "Now can be when we turn it around!" but it also guarantees that the player who is winning for most of the game can suddenly find themself on the short side of the stick.

RATING: N/A
survival horror board game that pits small-town Heroes head-to-head against a limitless horde of Zombies (players can play on the Hero team or as the Zombies). A modular board randomly determines the layout of the town at the start of each game and there are several different scenarios to play, adding lots of replayability. Fast Paced Game Play with Easy To Learn rules allows players to jump right into the action, while Strategic Depth and Strong Cooperative Play keeps the game interesting. To achieve a horror movie feel, all of the art for the game is photographic and the game comes with a CD Soundtrack of original music.Category: Horror, Fighting, Miniatures;  Mechanics: Co-operative Play, Hand Management, Dice Rolling, Variable Player Powers, Modular Board; expanded by: Growing Hunger, 'Stock Up' Supplement, Last Night on Earth Special Edition Soundtrack CD   
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Blech.  Too much take that, too much randomness, too much chaos.  Give me a game that's all one of those things, in a short play time, and I'll be fine.  Give me another, where the luck of the card draw means that the zombie player wins on turn FOUR by killing two folks, and I'll happily pass to play something a little more controlled.  I imagine the game would improve with someone actually explaining the game before leaping headlong into over-eager slaughter of the humans, but only slightly.

UPDATE: The game DOES improve when someone is willing to explain the rules to you, and if you go into the game with the knowledge that this is an experience game with some strategy, tactics, and Take That!, then it much improves the game.  If nothing else, the game creates a great narrative, and leads to some session reports that are far too much fun to read.  I might even have to pick this one up at some point.

3 plays: 5 players

Last Night on Earth, The Zombie Game is a survival horror board game that pits small-town Heroes head-to-head against a limitless horde of Zombies (players can play on the Hero team or as the Zombies). A modular board randomly determines the layout of the town at the start of each game and there are several different scenarios to play, adding lots of replayability. Fast Paced Game Play with Easy To Learn rules allows players to jump right into the action, while Strategic Depth and Strong Cooperative Play keeps the game interesting.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Great production value for a start-up game publisher, this game looks like it was put out by one of the big guys. The L-shaped tiles are a nice feature, allowing for a fair bit of board diversity from game to game and the miniatures are extremely well done. There are three different zombie sculpts and a unique, nicely detailed model for each hero. As an added bonus, everything is pre-punched so you can jump right into the action. The cards are fun, with super cheesy action shots featuring Man (or shotgun packing babe) vs. Zombie. Overall, it does a great job of setting the tone for an evening of zombie killing fun.

I'll admit that mechanically, it's not a game for everyone. Last Night on Earth can sometimes be a gigantic pile of randomness, and control freaks will want to pull their hair out. Many scenarios require the heroes to mill through their deck in search of key items to win the game. If those cards happen to be at the bottom of the deck, they lose. If they are at the top of the deck, they win. There is very little either side can do to affect the outcome when this occurs. Fortunately, this is fairly rare. When it does happen, the game is short enough to just have a laugh and play again. 

Combat is handled as it should be, zombies fall in droves to firearms, but become quite dangerous in close quarters. The system does a good job of representing the genre, giving the heroes every advantage in out-maneuvering and fending of the undead, but it does an equally good job of making a close encounter with a zombie swarm a very dangerous game.

My wife and I enjoy Last Night on Earth much more than the rest of our gaming group. We also own just about every zombie movie ever made, so clearly this game has more appeal for fans of the genre than it does for competitive gamers. It's random, dicey, and a touch simplistic. It's also the best Zombie game ever made, period. (Not that Zombie games are a big market share or anything...Basically, this game kicks the crap out of Zombies! and Zombietown.)

One of my all-time favorites...

Immersive theme, player(s) vs. player(s), and good balance make it a great game if you don't mind the luck of some dice rolling.  The only complaints I have are the cheesy dice (which I replaced with nice Chessex ones, and crap-for-made-in-China plastic cards (which is like trying to shuffle rigid Saran wrap).  The figures are very nice as are the boards and tokens.  I can even live with the photo-realistic cards are and the CD music which is at least original and won't offend.  My honest rating of this game is in the hight 8's to low 9's for fun factor, replay ability, and theme but my rating here is a 10 to counter act the few retards that have found their way to a keyboard and don't know the meaning of a "1" rating, especially when comparing this to other zombie games on the market today.  Hopefully FFG will do new scenarios and additional boards for this game.  A Shawn of the Dead scenario would be great.  If you're a zombies fan, the bottom line is get this game.  If you like cooperative games, this holds true also (though someone will need to play the zombies).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Perfect game in my opinion!  Great with large groups!  Always intense.  Perfect theme!  I've played this well over 200 times and there is plenty of strategy involved. In fact, I would say it has more strategy than many of the top games where your toughest choice is, "Should I take wood or stone" (games I definitely enjoy mind you).  Of course people who don't like any luck with immediately mock this rating.  They are forgetting that games are for fun and sometimes you want things to be a little random...dice aren't evil and neither are card draws.  You can control quite a bit in this game, but not everything and that's part of what makes this game a blast to play.  There are many different scenarios to play and lots of expansions which give a TON of replayability. The best thing about this game is that it is like a tool box for games.  You are given extra pieces to create your own games and scenarios...which I have done. I would recommend this game to anyone who loves theme and exciting/tense dice battles. The only downside is the rule book isn't written very well.  Be patient with that!

RATING: 8
Combining the best elements of several other zombies games, this one finally gets the undead theme right. Part quality is beyond belief (boards are a little cheap though). Expect LOTS of card playing. Seriously, this is not one of those games where players hold on to important cards until they are absolutly needed. Nope, chances are that zombie player is going to start zonking you with all sorts of cards the very first time you dare wander into a zombie space. Killing zombies is actually kind of difficult (you have to roll doubles) but keep in mind that's without weapons, and as long as you roll higher than the zombie you manage to push them off of you. Some may be dissapointed that the zombies can walk through wall, but I think games would get kind of stale if they couldn't. The rules themselves are fine, but the sheer number of cards in the game twist things up just enough to require a 30-some page FAQ sheet. Sigh. Kind of a drag, but this is still a real surprise. I'm not really sure the human player can EVER win some of the scenarios.

RATING: 6
Played through most of the scenarios.  Some are harder for one side than the other, and strategy is a must if you want a shot at winning from the more difficult side.  
Pros:
This game is very teachable, even to non-gamers.  The music is very appropriate and a great alternative to the hum of soda machines.  All of the scenarios (that I've played) are great fun, especially with a group that likes theme.  The pieces are great, even if you have to peel the cards off of each other when you first get the game.  Just long enough to build and create a great amount of tension. FFP seems very eager to offer new scenarios online!
Cons: 
Some of the zombie cards do little to nothing (adding "Strange" as descriptor, discarding 10 cards, being unable to trade) and seem to be more appropriate for a slightly different set of cards.  The heroes seem to be more prone to getting screwed by the dice than the zombies (but it's so hard to screw them such that they can't get back from it).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is my favorite zombie game ever!  

I really like the production value of this game.  A lot of planning went into this release and it shows!

Flying Frog Productions has one of the best customer service departments I have ever had to use.  Although it mainly consists of MaryBeth, they are on the right track of becoming one of the best game producers out there!

The game play for LNoE is outstanding on all accounts!  Not only is it a blast to play as either the zombies or heroes, but so much is going on here!  

The theme is implemented in everything and I think that is fantastic!  Anywhere from game events to strategy, I actually feel as though I am in a B horror movie during play.

The cards are great!  Some pretty excellent resources are available to heroes and very much play into the theme flawlessly.  Heroes find items that one would expect when trying to avoid a horde of brain-seeking mutants!

The game board is very unique in that it is consists of L-shaped mini boards to create a larger playing surface.  An addition of more playing boards will be  included in the Growing Hunger expansion and I hope to see a variety more in upcoming releases!

The game components are next to perfect.  Many complain that the cards are too thick and stick together, but I honestly like them a lot and haven't run into too many problems.  The artwork is excellent... what a unique way to depict items and game events through the actual use of actors!  

The miniatures are some of the best in comparison to every game I own and love!  Not only are they easily some of the most intricately detailed that exist, but they very much look exactly like the actual characters depicted on the Hero sheets!

The chits are top-notch as well. The glossy finish has to be the nicest touch of all, in my opinion.  This makes for a very durable game and one which will last many years to come!

I cannot be happier.  No other zombie-themed game comes remotely close to this!  This has to be the best available!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
Contrary to popular belief, this is not the best zombie game ever, not by a long shot. It may be the best zombie game 'released' but, come on, the competition isn't exactly challenging now is it?!

LNoE is an overrated popular mass market offering. [url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/game/27736]DEAD OF NIGHT[/url] and [url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/game/7514]ZOMBIE PLAGUE[/url], which are both games done by enthusiasts, and are both free PDF downloads, knock the living shit out of this steaming turd.

 LNoE attempts to utilise the best ideas from both of these games yet only manages to break them in the process!

[b]A constantly growing Forum of Rule Queries (over 1000 questions), presents an excellent example of the never ending loopholes you will find in this 'sandbox'.[/b]

IMHO the Fan Boys are just blinded by the overproduction. Gloss & sculpts do not make for a good game, and the photo-shopped semi-realistic artwork with camp, unconvincing, cheesy, piss poor actor posing in mock horror is not my cup of char either I tell thee.

LNoE totally misses the thematic mark. Presenting us with some pathetically bad B-Movie attempt, Instead of trying to recreate the classic zombie films by George A. Romero & Lucio Fulci. It's as if the designers have never even seen a zombie film, and are making their own assumptions as to what possibly happens in these films.

The ruling for zombies ghost walking effortlessly through walls, and heroes being able to fire through walls is a terrible idea which totally removes any feeling of realism, tension, or claustrophobia from the game. They should have stuck to doors only, and placed an odd window in here & there.

The lame scenarios fail miserably at trying to portray any of the defensive/survival situations that crop up in the vast majority of zombie movies.

The roll and move mechanic also leaves something to be desired. Zombies can catch up with healthy humans due to dumb dice chucking.

Then there's the RANDOMNESS... [i][b]"OMFG is this random!!!!!"[/b][/i] Strategy, skill & tactics do not feature in this game [u]at all[/u], as every single decision relies purely on luck. Virtually no choices in the game are left to the player alone without massive turn altering factors from die rolling, and card playing galore being slapped on top of every situation, altering every possible outcome.

The music CD is a wasted opportunity. A pointless inclusion, which is entirely unsuitable for an accompanying 'so called horror' soundtrack. Featuring ill suited, up tempo Midi sounds which lack in any atmosphere, and fail miserably at adding any spice to the lame offering.

I find it incredibly irritating that the uneducated Fan Boys will tirelessly defend what is nothing but a [b]Card & Dice fest'[/b]. These folk have obviously only ever watched one slapstick zombie comedy movie, and on that basis constantly refer to zombies only eating Brains!

RATING: 8
Survive against the attacks of the Zombies and fulfill the objectif in a scenario. Slasher game with a special cinematic moments and artwork. Rules are simple but effective. The game uses photographs of actors to depict on the cards. Zombie killing fun. 

Beware this game has very annoying skip a turn etc take that cards which are totally frustrating. But on the other hand the game provided us already with a ton of hilarious moments too. So if you search for zombiegame that gives you a story to tell after you played it, this is the zombiegame to recommend.

RATING: 7
A more conventional game than Mall of Horror, but just as enjoyable from my perspective.  Beautiful components (the the box insert could be better), and a really class game.  It is possible to get screwed over by randomness, which stops this from being a classic, but ultimately, it's an amazingly fun, B-movie-esque romp through Zombie territory.  Very good.
